Debate Rages Among Nations over Whether to Adjourn the Disarmament Conference 27

Henderson Urges Germany to Return to the Conference; Litvinov Presents a Resolution

(Geneva) At the executive meeting of the Disarmament Conference at 3:40 PM today, the issue of whether the Disarmament Conference should adjourn immediately or continue discussions and broaden its objectives was debated. It was expected that there would be a fierce war of words between the two factions. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov, representing those in favor of continuing discussions, spoke first, presenting a resolution containing seven points: (1) The General Committee should immediately study the issue of mutual assistance pacts and the definition of "aggressor states." (2) The Disarmament Conference should immediately become a permanent peace conference and continue its work. (3) The conference, entrusted with this task, should maintain the same relationship with the League of Nations and continue to work to establish a compromise on a convention to reduce or limit armaments. (4) The conference should seek coordination or other plans to create new guarantees of security. (5) The conference should establish preventive plans to prevent armed conflicts. (6) The conference should supervise the implementation of the convention and the resolutions of the conference. (7) The conference should consult on countermeasures in the event of a breach of the treaty. The above seven points, as far as is currently known, will be supported by France, Poland, the Little Entente, and the Balkan countries. Britain, Italy, and Belgium are in favor of adjournment, and the United States is roughly the same. Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson, in summarizing the general situation at the meeting this afternoon, strongly urged the need to invite Germany back to the conference for discussions, and suggested a suitable method to entrust the executive branch with the task of reconciling differences. French Foreign Minister Barthou spoke sharply, saying that if Henderson's suggestion contained new avenues, he would oppose this principle unless he was carrying something in his luggage. It should be known that British disarmament salesman Eden had already traveled to many countries without success. What he regrets is that he is not yet proficient in the language of Geneva, so he is easily misunderstood. But he feels that many important proposals have been submitted to the executive branch, ready for discussion. For this reason, he opposes adjournment. (Reuters, 4th)

(Geneva) The Bureau of the Disarmament Conference will meet this afternoon to discuss the agenda of the General Assembly. According to reliable sources, the decision has been made to form a special committee in addition to the original two committees of the General Assembly to deal with security and disarmament issues. This approach is satisfactory to both Britain and France, and the Disarmament Conference can get a long rest. (National Telegram, 4th)

(Paris) According to a London dispatch received by Le Matin, some members of the British Cabinet intend to request Foreign Secretary Simon to return to Geneva to attend the Disarmament General Committee at today's emergency Cabinet meeting. It also said that former Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Eden was promoted to Lord Privy Seal for his contribution to the Disarmament Conference, and has now been promoted to Privy Councilor, which has a deeper meaning. League of Nations Administrative Council Passes Saar Report; Franco-German Declaration Guarantees Self-Determination Vote; Voting Results May Maintain the Status Quo 28

(Geneva) The International Saar Governing Commission's recommendation to hold a plebiscite on January 13 next year has been passed by the Administrative Council today. The report first details the current situation in the Saar region, and states that although there are some political movements there, the plebiscite scheduled for January in accordance with the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles should proceed smoothly. The report was drafted by Mr. Knox, the British Chairman of the Governing Commission. Before it was passed, anti-Hitler elements strongly opposed it, because they believed that a free and confidential reliable vote could not be held under the terrorist activities implemented by the German National Socialist Party, so it would be better to postpone it. After the report was passed, the Administrative Council stated that the League of Nations will proceed cautiously with the voting plan, because a slight oversight could easily lead to a Franco-German war. The Saar people's self-determination vote has three options: (1) Maintain the autonomous political system established by the Treaty of Versailles; (2) Merge with France; (3) Merge with Germany. Political observers today stated that the results of the plebiscite are now more difficult to predict than before. France's plan to appease the Saar people has not achieved much, but the people may not be completely in favor of merging with Germany, because there are many socialists and anti-Hitler elements in the area who are deeply afraid that their lives will be endangered after the merger. Therefore, there is a good chance that the voting results will maintain the autonomous system, which is especially desired by France, but others believe that the people will demand to merge with Germany. (National Telegram, 4th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council held a closed meeting this morning, and will change to an open meeting when discussing the Saar agreement. The League of Nations has no doubt that the Administrative Council will directly accept the Saar report without modification. However, French Foreign Minister Barthou will give a speech at that time, and the Administrative Council will also appoint the Saar People's Voting Committee. The committee will be established on July 1. The most likely candidates are Professor Beren of the University of Montreal, Director-General Roda of Sweden, and Administrative Commissioner de Puf of the Netherlands. Ms. Hua of the United States is said to be hired as an expert advisor. (National Telegram, 4th)

(Paris) A demonstration occurred in Saarbrücken, the capital of the Saar region, last night. The wife of Socialist leader Brown was insulted by National Socialist demonstrators. Le Petit Parisien reported on this matter today, saying that Brown, who is currently in Geneva, received the news and returned to Saarbrücken from Geneva today. Before leaving, he sent a long letter to French Foreign Minister Barthou, reporting the insult to his wife and saying that it is urgent and cannot be delayed for the French Foreign Minister to pay attention to it, take serious measures, and maintain order in the Saar. Le Petit Parisien also said that it is now certain that the League of Nations Administrative Council will hold a meeting tomorrow and issue a solemn warning to the National Socialist elements who instigated the disturbances, hoping that they will realize their mistakes. According to a Saarbrücken dispatch published by Le Petit Parisien, the Saar region's Communist Party has finally decided on its attitude towards the 1935 plebiscite.

The British Monarch Quietly Celebrates Birthday in the Palace 29

Yang Jie Attends Cavalry Review (London) Today is the sixty-ninth birthday of the British monarch. Only a small group of the royal family quietly celebrated at Buckingham Palace and received many congratulatory telegrams from foreign heads of state and various parts of the Empire. The formal celebration will be held tomorrow, and the monarch will attend a military parade to receive congratulations from the public. (Reuters, 3rd)

(London) A cavalry review was held today to celebrate the sixty-ninth birthday of the British monarch. The Chinese military delegation, led by Yang Jie, also attended the event. Mr. Yang and his party then went to visit the Vickers tank and aircraft factories. Tomorrow, the Chinese ambassador to the UK will accompany Yang Jie to meet with the British Secretary of State for War. On Saturday and Sunday, the Chinese military delegation will lay a wreath at the European War Memorial. (Reuters, 4th)

Until recently, the Communist Party leaders put forward slogans to their members, advocating that the Saar region should belong to the German Soviet Republic. However, the Treaty of Versailles stipulates that the plebiscite only has three options: maintaining the current system, belonging to Germany, or belonging to France. If votes are cast according to the Communist Party's slogans, they will be invalid. Therefore, the Communist Party, considering this point, has issued a proclamation ordering Saar Communist Party members to vote to maintain the current system. This decision is quite important because, in the Saar region, the Communist Party is the largest political party besides the old central party. In previous Saar parliamentary elections, the Communist Party has always obtained more than 60,000 votes. (Havas, 3rd)

(Geneva) The German guarantee issue for the Saar people's plebiscite to determine their own future on January 13th next year has been clearly stipulated in a declaration issued by the foreign ministers of France and Germany. The declaration has been sent to Mr. Aloisi, the Chairman of the Saar Territory Commission. Germany declared that it would not exert any direct or indirect pressure on the voting people. Regardless of the voters' attitude, Germany would never take retaliatory measures or coercion. If any dispute arises between Germany and any member of the League of Nations Council regarding the interpretation or implementation of this guarantee, Germany is willing to submit such dispute to the Hague International Court of Justice for adjudication. Germany also allows the League of Nations Commission to establish a Supreme Court for a period of one year after the vote. (National Telegram, 3rd)

(Geneva) At the meeting of the League of Nations Council on Monday morning, in addition to discussing the border incident between Hungary and Yugoslavia, it will also make a resolution on the Saar region's plebiscite issue. Regarding the preparations for the 1935 Saar region plebiscite, the League of Nations Council previously organized a three-person committee, chaired by Mr. Aloisi, the Italian representative, to be responsible for research. Subsequently, after consultations with the foreign ministers of France and Germany by the three-person committee, an agreement on the preparations for the Saar plebiscite was established. The three-person committee has drafted a report, listing the clauses of this agreement. The report has been distributed to the delegations of various countries attending the Council and to the press today. The report contains four draft resolutions, all of which will be voted on at the Council meeting on Monday. The contents of these draft resolutions are summarized as follows:

(1) Resolution on the date of the plebiscite: The plebiscite is scheduled to be held on Sunday, January 13, 1935. The Council reserves the right to consider, at an appropriate time, certain methods, so that the Saar residents without voting rights may also enjoy the benefits of the commitments made by the governments of France and Germany to the voters. The Council shall supervise the implementation of these commitments, as the implementation of these commitments is a major condition for the plebiscite.

(2) Resolution on the establishment of the Plebiscite Commission: The resolution proposes the establishment of a Plebiscite Commission and determines its due powers for the organization, management, and supervision of the plebiscite. For matters related to the plebiscite that are not within the prescribed powers of the Commission, the Commission may propose methods and request the League of Nations Council to approve them, or, in urgent situations, request the Council Committee to approve them. The Plebiscite Commission shall consist of three members, appointed by the Council. Another expert shall be appointed by the Council as the technical advisor to the Commission. The Saar Territory Government Committee shall prepare to assist the Plebiscite Commission and pay attention at all times to ensure that the Commission receives all necessary assistance and supplies from the Saar public authorities.

(3) Regulations on the results of the plebiscite and the establishment of the Plebiscite Court: The Council shall adopt rules stipulating that the results of the vote shall be decided jointly in each locality. The Council will also decide to establish a Plebiscite Court and eight sub-courts in each polling district. Lawsuits regarding voter registration and criminal cases related to the plebiscite shall be tried by this court. The Plebiscite Commission shall determine the date on which the court begins to serve.

(4) Special resolution on maintaining public order: The Council allows the Saar Government Committee to increase the number of police officers if necessary, by recruiting them from outside Saar residents or transferring necessary police personnel. The Council is prepared to approve this. The three-person committee believes that it is beneficial for the Council to request League of Nations member states to recruit personnel to serve as police and local constables in the Saar region for the convenience of the Saar Government Committee. Regarding the expenses required for the plebiscite, the Saar Government Committee shall allocate 1 million francs before July 1, and the governments of France and Germany shall each allocate 5 million francs.

In addition to the above draft resolutions, the report of the three-person committee also includes a letter from Baron Aloisi, Chairman of the Committee, to the governments of France and Germany, requesting the two governments to solemnly declare to the Council their firm will to fulfill all obligations arising from the treaty, and to present the government measures and special procedures prepared for the implementation of these obligations. Subsequently, French Foreign Minister Barthou and German Foreign Minister Neurath jointly prepared a letter on June 2, replying to Baron Aloisi. The letter stated that the two governments agreed to eliminate all kinds of oppression that could hinder the freedom of voting, and that the people entitled to vote in the Saar region would not be prosecuted or discriminated against because of their political attitude during the League of Nations' rule. In addition, beneficial measures will be taken to prohibit the actions of nationals who violate the above commitments. If any dispute arises between France, Germany, and a country attending the League of Nations Council regarding the implementation of the above commitments, the governments of the countries concerned agree to submit the dispute to the Hague International Court of Arbitration for resolution. Furthermore, the governments of France and Germany recognize a transitional period of one year from the date of the establishment of the Saar region's ruling system. During the transitional period, the Senior Plebiscite Court will continue to exist. Anyone entitled to vote in the Saar region, who has suffered oppression or retaliation due to their political attitude related to the plebiscite during the League of Nations' rule of the Saar, may file a complaint with the Senior Court. In the event of criminal and administrative litigation outside the Saar territory, anyone entitled to vote in the Saar may request the Plebiscite Court to determine whether the litigation violates the country's commitments, etc. In addition, the report of the three-person committee also pointed out that there is obviously no distinction between men and women and nationality in the right to vote in the Saar region. Anyone who is 20 years old on the voting date and has resided in the Saar region since June 28, 1919, has the right to vote. (Havas, 4th)

New French Military Exercises 32

(Paris) Previously, French reservists were convened separately in various localities during exercise periods, and no large-scale exercises were ever held with many troops gathered in one place. According to Le Journal, the method of reservist exercises will be greatly changed this year. From September 15th to 30th, 15,000 reservists will be formed into a division, fully equipped for wartime, just like during mobilization. The exercise site will be in the Champagne province, and the commander of the exercise will be General Bretelats, commander of the Paris garrison. He made the following remarks to a reporter from Le Journal: "This exercise is a partial mobilization method, which has never been tested before. This plan has been in place since 1926, but it has been delayed for eight years due to lack of funding. As you know, when the European War began in 1914, General Joffre lacked fully trained reservist troops, while the German reservists mobilized for combat had received training as complete as that of active-duty soldiers. After the lessons of that year, we cannot but pay attention to the reservists. We can rely on How many reservists are there in our country? After the exercise in September this year, we will know." Le Journal concluded that the gathering of 15,000 reservists for exercises should not be regarded as France flexing its muscles. "When the situation on the east bank of the Rhine is getting tense, we must prepare for a rainy day in case of emergency. Our national defense organization is based on trained reservists, so we must first test the combat capabilities of our reservists." (Havas, 4th)

International Labour Conference Opens, Elects Committee to Protect Workers' Interests; Labour Bureau Staff to Be Expanded 33

(Geneva) The 18th International Labour Conference opened this morning and publicly elected French Senator and former Labour Minister Godart as the chairman of the conference. (Central News Agency, 4th)

(Geneva) The International Labour Bureau conference opened at 11 o'clock this morning and elected French Senator Godart as chairman. The procedures of the conference are (1) the Saar region issue; (2) the election of a committee to protect workers' interests. (Reuters, 4th) (Geneva) The Labour Conference opened here today. Representatives from 46 countries, including the United Kingdom and the United States, are participating in the conference, and former French Labour Minister Godart was elected chairman of this International Labour Conference. Mr. Godart is also one of the initiators of the conference. (National Telegram, 4th)

(Geneva) A proposal to increase the staff of the International Labour Bureau from 24 to 32 was submitted at today's conference by representatives of Denmark and Argentina. Argentina also requested the approval of the amendment to Article 393 of the Treaty of Versailles. (National Telegram, 4th)

(Geneva) The International Labour Conference opens here tomorrow, and issues closely related to the world's workers will be discussed. 50 countries have sent representatives to participate, including the United States. The United States is not a member of the League of Nations, and will send official observers from its labor, capital, and government sectors to attend. Labour leaders are deeply convinced that the United States will soon join the International Labour Bureau. There are still two major industrial countries that have not joined the International Labour Bureau, namely Germany and Soviet Russia. Germany withdrew last year, and Soviet Russia has never joined. Important figures in the International Labour Bureau are deeply afraid that after Japan's economic aggression is severely attacked at this conference, Japan may withdraw. The Japanese side does not deny the possibility of this, but says that this move depends entirely on whether the Japanese representatives can overturn various rumors from the outside world. When the conference opens, representatives from various countries will review the work of the International Labour Bureau. At this time, the British representatives may rise up to criticize Japanese wages. In addition to this, there are no other points in the agenda that attack Japan. The first step of the conference is to re-elect the administrative staff. There are currently 24 administrative staff, of which 12 are government representatives, 6 are worker representatives, and 6 are capital representatives. It is now planned to increase the number to 32, "16 government representatives, 8 labor and capital representatives each," so that countries outside of Europe, such as South America, can also send representatives. The main agenda item is the plan to alleviate world unemployment. The International Labour Bureau knows that the United Kingdom spent £107,000,000 to help the unemployed last year, and the United States spent about US$1,000,000,000, and both countries are willing to shorten the weekly working hours to 40 hours and promote large-scale public works to reduce unemployment. Supporters of the 40-hour work system will urge the final reading of the 40-hour work system draft, which has been discussed before, but it is not believed that it can be passed due to British opposition to the conference. Labour experts said that this draft does not conflict with the new American business rules, so although the American representatives have no voting rights, they are expected to support this draft. French representatives will call for international action on public works as a way to alleviate unemployment. The International Labour Bureau has recently applied to various countries to build public works to reduce unemployment. Although Germany is no longer a member, the International Labour Bureau has given much encouragement to the effects of German public works. According to official reports, German public works cost a total of 100,000,000 marks, of which 57% has been paid for by the public works themselves. There are three costs: (1) the reduction of unemployment relief costs; (2) the increase of the unemployment insurance fund; (3) the increase of tax revenue. It is said that those who oppose reducing working hours and building public works will express their views at this conference. British workers support this plan. This plan was originally proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. The conference will also give a final reading to the draft on unemployment insurance and other assistance to unemployed workers. American representatives are particularly interested in this draft because the United States does not have this labour law. The meeting will last for two weeks. Government and labour representatives are in an equal position in the conference. (National News Agency, 3rd)

Roosevelt Returns to Capital to Mediate Labour Disputes 34

(New York) President Roosevelt returned to Washington today to face the most difficult issue under the National Recovery Act. 300,000 steel and lead workers are demanding (1) recognition of collective bargaining; (2) a 30-hour work week; and (3) higher standard wages, claiming that if these demands are not accepted, they will strike on June 15. Many of the workers' leaders are radical elements. Even if the steelworkers' union cancels the strike because it has the right to participate in the Steel Labour Bureau, other workers' leaders may still have to resist. President Roosevelt is now in a situation where he has no choice but to intervene. (Reuters, 4th)

The Toledo electric company and the leaders of the striking workers signed an agreement yesterday afternoon, and one of the most intense labour disputes in American labour history has now been resolved. This agreement stipulates a 5% wage increase, recognition of the workers' union, and stipulates that all disputes in the future will be resolved through negotiations between the two parties. The number of power plant strikers totalled 5,000. There was a group attack on the power plant, and there were clashes with the military police, resulting in the death of three people and injuries to some people. (Reuters, 4th)

Chaos in Japanese Politics: Takahashi Plays a Crucial Role; No Suitable Person to Form a Cabinet 42

(Tokyo) The Saito Cabinet is now quietly observing the state of government transition, but this quiet observation will be broken by the report of Justice Minister Koyama on the Kuroda issue, and the timing is gradually approaching. Although opinions on the political situation vary due to different positions, the view that a political change is coming is completely unanimous. The advance and retreat of the Saito Cabinet will be triggered by the resignation of Finance Minister Takahashi. (Daily News Agency, 4th)

(Tokyo) The political situation has temporarily eased due to the death of Marshal Togo, but behind-the-scenes activities in various aspects are still intense. According to the observations of influential figures in the Peerage Council, the truth about the Kuroda Vice-Minister issue is gradually becoming clear. Prime Minister Saito, Finance Minister Takahashi, and Navy Minister Yamamoto also seem to have decided to advance and retreat. Therefore, although the government is working hard to promote the reconstruction of the cabinet and continue to serve, the general trend does not allow its existence. If the content of Justice Minister Koyama's report on the Kuroda issue has the nature of malfeasance, then Finance Minister Takahashi will naturally resign. Takahashi's resignation is the fatal blow to the current cabinet. Therefore, the political change will occur approximately 15 days after the Koyama report. Although Governor Ugaki has the strength to succeed the cabinet, the Navy's statement the other day has some impact on Ugaki. Although Count Kiyoura is an important figure in the political world, he must travel to avoid the cold every winter due to his old age, which is inconvenient for attending parliament. Therefore, whether the Kiyoura cabinet theory is powerful is quite questionable. As for the Hiranuma cabinet theory, it does not attract public attention at present. In short, Japan currently has no suitable person to succeed the cabinet. It is still appropriate to regard Ugaki as the most powerful person to succeed the cabinet. On the political party side, they are taking advantage of the high tide of "political change is coming" to carry out activities. The Seiyukai, with President Suzuki as the center, plans to realize the cooperative cabinet of the Seiyukai and Minseito parties. If the imperial order to form a cabinet does not fall on Suzuki, then it opposes any cabinet theory. The Kuwabara faction is quite openly supporting the Kiyoura cabinet, and the Tokonami faction is also connected with Kuwabara, and is also in contact with the Minseito party, but their attitude is not very clear and they adopt opportunism. The Seiyukai's internal affairs are so complicated. If a political change comes, internal disturbances will inevitably occur. The Minseito party believes that the emergence of a political party cabinet is completely hopeless, and has no intention of realizing the joint cabinet theory with the Seiyukai, but Ugaki has always had a close relationship with the Minseito party, so its leaders secretly support Ugaki in winning power. (Daily News Agency, 4th)

Sichuan Army Thoroughly Suppresses Communist Bandits 97

Finding Ways to Attack the Mind, Causing the Bandits' Internal Collapse; Grasping the People, Cutting off the Bandits' Lifeline. Chengdu Correspondence: Recently, the Communist bandit forces in northern Sichuan have gradually become exhausted. The bandit leader, Xu Xiangqian, once fell ill due to resentment, and since then his nature has become even more violent. He is stubborn and opinionated in everything, and the divisive forces within his ranks are spreading more and more fiercely. Although he frequently launches surprise attacks on the positions of the 2nd, 3rd, 4th, and 6th Route Armies of the National Army, attempting to break the encirclement, he has suffered repeated heavy blows due to the strict precautions taken by each army. The 3rd Route Army recently captured Zhou Ziming, a platoon leader of the bandits, and others. According to their confessions, "When the bandit Xu entered Sichuan, he led four divisions of men. After occupying Tongjiang, he reorganized them into the pseudo 4th, 9th, 30th, and 31st and 4th Armies. He Wei, the commander of the pseudo 9th Army, was wounded and died in Yilong from shrapnel from a bomb, and was buried in Yingge Mouth. Most of the old bandits have died. The bandit army adopts a three-three system, but each regiment has only 600 men, and each gun is equipped with six clips of ammunition. Recently, they have been blockaded by the government army, and ammunition is scarce. Only the old bandits have a dozen bullets each, and salt is the most scarce."

According to headquarters intelligence, the 5th Route Army has divided its forces in recent days to assist the 4th and 6th Routes, engaging in fierce battles with the bandits many times, killing many bandits. There have been daily reports of bandits at the front bringing their weapons and surrendering. Liu Xiang has issued orders to all routes to widely open the path to surrender, not to investigate the past. Yesterday, Xu Yaoqing, commander of the 5th Route Army, sent a long telegram to Liu, the commander-in-chief, all commanders, and the Pacification Committee, stating his opinions on bandit suppression, saying that if bandits are to be eliminated as soon as possible, military and political measures must be combined to be effective. He recounted various facts and experiences he had gained at the front as evidence, and every word had a source and was very valuable. Therefore, I have excerpted a summary of it as follows: "Since the joint forces of all routes began suppressing bandits, more than eight months have passed without complete success. Although officers and soldiers have fought hard and repeatedly defeated the fierce bandits, the bandit area has shrunk, and their strength has become concentrated. Recently, they have relied on natural barriers to resist stubbornly. If we do not find ways to attack their minds and cause their internal collapse, relying solely on military force will make it difficult to eliminate them in the short term. This is why Chairman Chiang has instructed that bandit suppression should be three parts military and seven parts political. I lead troops to suppress bandits and have fought fiercely until now. I deeply feel that military and political measures must be combined to have any hope of eliminating them. Recently, I investigated the recovered areas and found that there is no political clean-up being carried out. Everything is merely superficial. We must know that we must prescribe the right medicine for the illness without delay, so as to avoid future troubles. I would like to briefly state to you gentlemen what I have seen and heard. The Red bandits purely use deceptive means to lure the people, and they fully utilize ignorant villagers and local bullies to serve as chairmen, representatives, or committee members. They try their best to get them to implicate local wealthy gentlemen, civil servants, and middle-class families, confiscate their property, and kill their families, so that they will bear grudges against each other. They slightly divide the land and give it to the poor to show their favor. Furthermore, they select the cunning ones among the poor and accuse them of reactionary crimes or secretly protecting wealthy gentlemen, killing one or two of them to show their power. Therefore, the general poor people all follow them to the death, not daring to leave or rebel without exerting themselves. They also order them to break family relationships and search and kill them first. All the 'reddened' poor people in the recovered bandit areas are afraid of being investigated by the government and even more afraid of revenge from their fellow villagers, so they have no choice but to follow the bandits. Once they are incorporated into the bandit ranks, they are trained day and night, or they are told that the government troops will brutally kill them if they surrender, to strengthen their resolve. They also fabricate rumors, not mentioning how Chengdu and Chongqing are doing, but saying how Dongchuan is doing, and how the Red Army is winning, exaggerating and exaggerating to frighten them. Therefore, those who are forced to become bandits know that the Communist bandits are brutal and inhumane, and they are eager to escape, but they are afraid of bearing grudges in their hometowns, having no home to return to, and they are also misled by the government troops' brutal killings, so they do not dare to surrender. There is no way forward or backward, and they only seek to die quickly. Although the army tries its best to spread propaganda, they are still facing each other and do not dare to believe it deeply. As for the leaflets distributed by airplanes, many bandits are illiterate and are afraid of their tyrannical power, so they do not dare to pick them up and look at them, as if they are lost in a fog and do not know what is going on. Although there have been bandits surrendering in recent days, the number is very small. They all say that they wanted to escape and surrender long ago, but they were ultimately misled by the above situation and did not dare to try easily. Now that the various routes are encircling them, the bandit forces are exhausted, food is scarce, and the bandits' hearts are scattered. The best method for now is to have the counties and townships quickly form a joint public propaganda and security post-disaster committee to go to the front lines of the various armies, divisions, regiments, and brigades, and loudly proclaim to the bandits day and night that they are all fellow Sichuanese, why bother abandoning their wives and children and sacrificing themselves for the bandits, causing their society and families to be ruined? Furthermore, if the government troops advance to suppress them, they will either die from gunfire or be killed by the bandits. They should repent as soon as possible, either scatter and escape home, or bring their weapons and surrender. It is decided to issue certificates of protection and provide travel expenses to allow them to return alive. As for all kinds of grudges with the local people in the past, they will not be investigated. A deadline is set for them to return, otherwise, they will be regarded as willingly following the bandits and will not be tolerated, and their families will be investigated. If this can be done, the bandits' hearts will be scattered, and they will collapse immediately, so that the bandits will have no way to seize the people to create chaos, and it will not be difficult to eliminate them in one fell swoop. We must know that persuading the bandits is the way to clear them, and saving people is the way to save ourselves. I hope that you gentlemen will act quickly to achieve this." (National News Agency)

The Establishment of Linquan County in Northern Anhui 98

The county seat is located in Shenqiu Settlement. The Department of Civil Affairs sends personnel to prepare. Anqing Correspondence: Fuyang County in northern Anhui is vast, and the establishment of a new county seat has been brewing for a long time. Recently, the General Headquarters for Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, based on the request of the Sui Jing Commissioner's Office in Henan, military agencies, and local organizations, to establish a new county in the western territory of Fuyang, ordered the Anhui Provincial Government to investigate and report. Subsequently, the Anhui Provincial Government ordered Zang Dezhi, a member of the Department of Civil Affairs, to go to Fuyang to conduct an on-site survey and submit a report, which was reviewed and forwarded by the Department of Civil Affairs. It was considered that the western territory of Fuyang was far from the county seat, bordering Henan Province, and it was difficult to govern the banditry that had been rampant for many years. The establishment of a new county was in line with the outline of the administrative regional reorganization method promulgated by the Ministry. Therefore, three matters were carefully reviewed and approved: (1) For the sake of the situation and economy, the county seat was decided to be located in Shenqiu Settlement; (2) The area where the new county borders the northern section of Fuyang should still be bounded by the ancient ditch to conform to the natural terrain; (3) The name of the county was determined to be Linquan County. The matter was submitted to the 237th discussion meeting of the provincial government on May 29 and was approved. The preparations for the establishment of the county were also listed item by item, and Zhang Guohua, director of the second section of the fourth department of the Department of Civil Affairs, was appointed as the preparation officer for the establishment of the new county. He was ordered to immediately go and follow the resolutions and instructions of various methods, and cooperate with Fuyang County to quickly prepare and report. The preparation office was limited to be established before July 1, and all start-up fees and travel expenses were set at 1,000 yuan, and the monthly salary and office expenses were set at 800 yuan, and the Department of Finance was ordered to allocate funds. Anhui Province has recently transferred Yingshan to Hubei and newly established Huang Jia Shan and Liang Counties. Originally, there were a total of 61 counties. Now that a new county has been added in western Fuyang, the province governs a total of 62 counties. (4th)

Guangdong Province Sugar Monopoly 100

Thirteen sugar public warehouses are established in various prefectures. Sales operators and distributors are set up to promote sales. Guangzhou Correspondence: The Sugar Department of the Guangdong Provincial National Goods Promotion Office recently decided to implement a sugar control method for the purpose of promoting domestic products, as the state-run sugar factories in Huizhou Panyu Xinzhao have been established one after another and can produce 2,000 dan of sugar per month (100 jin per dan). The method will be implemented on the 1st of this month. According to the method, 20,000 dan of refined white sugar will be prepared for exclusive sales. Ten well-known sugar shops will be selected as sugar operators for the whole province to form a joint office, and a deposit of 40,000 yuan must be paid as a guarantee that they will comply with the regulations and promote sales. The Sugar Department will establish thirteen sugar public warehouses in various prefectural towns, and the sugar operators will set up 240 distributors within the scope of each public warehouse to act as agents for sales. Each distributor must sell at least 100 dan of cane sugar per month and pay a deposit of 300 yuan. The money will be deposited in the bank and earn interest at 6% per annum. The agency sales period is set at four months as a trial period. If the operation is properly handled, the contract may be renewed. If the distributor can sell 100 dan of sugar per month, a deposit of 300 yuan must be paid as a guarantee that the sugar industry will be promoted in accordance with the regulations of the provincial government and that private sugar will not be bought or sold. Each prefectural public warehouse is managed by a director appointed by the National Goods Promotion Office, who is responsible for all warehouse affairs such as sugar storage and shipment, and supervises the business operators and agents within the scope of the warehouse to promote the sale of state-run cane sugar and the conclusion of business matters. The joint office of various sugar merchants in the provincial capital was established today (the 1st), and the various regulations of the National Goods Promotion Office on sugar control will also be implemented from this day. As for the sugar business control rules, in general, if sugar produced by sugar factories in this province is transported out of the factory, a factory exit permit must be obtained from the Sugar Department of the National Goods Promotion Office before it can be shipped out, otherwise it will be regarded as private transportation. If imported sugar is imported, the operator must obtain an import permit from the Sugar Department before it can be imported. Sugar stored in public warehouses after obtaining a permit must apply for a transport and sales permit before it can be transported. If imported sugar and sugar from this province are to be transported out of the province, an exit permit must also be obtained. From the date of establishment of the Sugar Department, sugar stored by sugar merchants must be registered, and a delivery note must be issued for retail sugar of more than five jin, otherwise it will be regarded as private sugar. The quantity of modified imported sugar exceeding 300 jin must still be stored in the public warehouse. Anyone who commits private transportation will be dealt with in accordance with the regulations of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Office of the Finance Department. (June 1)

Completion of the Highway in the Border Area of the Three Provinces of Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Anhui 104

The Wu-Bai Road is scheduled to open to traffic. The Tun-Jing section will start construction soon. Wuyuan Correspondence: The highways in the border area of the three provinces of Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Anhui, including the main lines from Jingde to Leping Wannian, Qu County to Changshan Kaihua, and Tunxi via Qimen to Jingde, except for the Jing-Tun line which has not yet been built, the Jiangxi and Zhejiang lines have been built and opened to traffic. However, the two major sections connecting Anhui Province from Wuyuan to Dexing and Baishaguan to Wuyuan were previously slow in construction, which prevented the highways in the border area of the three provinces of Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui from being connected. Chairman Chiang, recognizing that the construction of the Wu-Bai and Wu-De sections is of utmost importance to the transportation of the three provinces, repeatedly ordered Zeng Yangfu, director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, to form the Zhejiang-Jiangxi-Anhui Border Highway Engineering Office to actively speed up construction. Since construction began five months ago, although the mountains and rocks are dangerous and the project is huge, the progress is still fast. All the bridges, culverts, and road surfaces have been completed in the middle of this month. Director Zeng of the Highway Office not only reported to Chairman Chiang by telegram, but also made early preparations for the opening of the Wu-Bai Road, and scheduled the opening ceremony to be held on June 4 at the station outside the West Gate of Wucheng. Zeng Yangfu, director of the Zhejiang Construction Department and director of the Highway Office, and Zhao Guantao, commander of the four provinces' garrison, will all come to Wuyuan to participate. County Magistrate Liu has been preparing everything, and on the previous day, he led Jiang Youbai and other members of the Highway Committee to inspect the Wu-Bai Road, and ordered the unfinished projects to be completed before June 4, so as to open to traffic as scheduled. From then on, transportation in the three provinces will become much more convenient. As for the two main lines from Tunxi to Jingde and the Tun-Yin section of the Wu-Yin Road, the surveying has been completed and construction will begin soon. (May 31)

General Situation of Drug Distribution in Jiangsu Province 105

For six years, the poisonous fog has filled the province. In addition to opium, red pills are the most common. Zhenjiang News: The ban on opium in Jiangsu Province, from the second half of the 17th year to June of the 27th year, in these six years, the initial period was the period when opium was prevalent. The sources were the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, the coastal ports, and the areas bordering Shandong, Henan, and Anhui. At that time, anesthetic drugs were only found in Yixing and Liyang. After the 19th year, the power gradually extended to the counties of Nantong and Rudong in northern Jiangsu. The popularity of drug pills is no less than that in southern Jiangsu. Heroin is also increasing in the Xuhai area, especially red pills, which are the most common. The manufacturing institutions for these red pills initially sought refuge in concessions, but have recently gradually moved inland. Those who are particularly cunning set up machines in boats and travel around, secretly manufacturing and selling them. Unscrupulous military police also provide protection from them. As a result, the scourge of drugs has spread and cannot be controlled. Currently, this province adopts a gradual policy for opium addicts, ordering them to gradually reduce the amount each year until it is completely banned in four years. For drug offenders, strict measures are used, and manufacturers and traffickers are punished with extreme penalties, and addicts are also dealt with by military law. All regulations and methods have been submitted to Chairman Chiang for approval and implementation. Recently, the Interim Regulations on Strictly Prohibiting Highly Addictive Drugs have been promulgated. The provincial and county opium prohibition committees will also be established one after another. (4th)

Jiang Song went to offer incense and pray for blessings, but died tragically 106

Shen Xitao and others from Songyi who believed in Buddha joined together to offer incense and recite Buddha's name, in order to pray for blessings. This time, Shen initiated the event of going to Mount Wutai to offer incense, gathering more than a dozen people to go north together. Recently, his family received news that the group encountered bandits in Dingzhou and was robbed, losing more than 1,000 yuan. Shen Xitao was shot and killed by bandits for unknown reasons. The local government authorities inspected and collected the body, arrested the murderers, and notified the family members to consult. Shen's family members cried bitterly after hearing the news.

Appointed Opium Prohibition Committee Members 107

The county government previously received instructions from the provincial government to organize an opium prohibition committee for the four-year prohibition plan, with the county and public chiefs as ex officio members, and three local people were appointed as committee members. Kunshan Commemorates Opium Prohibition and Burns Drugs 108

Yesterday was Opium Prohibition Day. All city agencies, groups, and schools gathered at the public gymnasium at 9:00 a.m. to hold a commemorative meeting. More than 5,000 people attended. Chairman Peng Baichuan reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by speeches by representatives of various agencies. Finally, they paraded in a line around the city and dispersed. At noon, the county government burned the drugs seized over the past year, such as opium, opium utensils, and red pills, in front of the auditorium. Yu Dianfen, chief of the first section of the Wuxi County Civil Affairs Department, and Xu Jichang, an investigator from the Wujiang County High Court, were commissioned to Kunshan to supervise. Representatives from various agencies in the city were sent to the scene to observe. The two commissioners inspected 170 pieces of opium utensils and 380,000 red pills one by one to ensure that there were no errors, stacked them in front of the hall, poured kerosene on them, took photos, and then set them on fire. The burning was completed at one o'clock.

Jiading Security Team Soldiers Tease Women, Causing Public Outrage 109

In Nanxiang Town, Jiading County, a New Life Movement lantern festival was held from the 1st, which was very lively. Qian Jinsheng, an employee of the Stamp Department of the Shanghai Postal Administration, led his mother, Huang, and wife, Lai, to Xiang. At about 8:00 p.m., they were watching under the lantern shed at Xianghua Bridge in Zhongshi. Xing Longnian, a soldier from the sixth squadron of the Shanghai Security Team stationed at the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Station in the town, also went to Xianghua Bridge to watch the lanterns. He caught sight of Lai and immediately stepped forward to tease her. He repeatedly groped Lai up and down in the crowd. Lai scolded him, and Xing retorted with insults. Lai's husband, Qian Jinsheng, stepped forward to negotiate, and Xing hit him with the leather strap he was holding. Lai stepped forward to protect him and was kicked multiple times in the lower body. Lai was six months pregnant and immediately fainted. The onlookers shouted to stop him, but Xing hit them indiscriminately with his leather belt. The crowd was furious and beat Xing into an injury. Qian, fearing trouble, tried his best to dissuade them and ordered his son, Huang Xiangsheng, and others to twist Xing and help Lai to the town's public security bureau to request a ruling. Wang Xingyuan, the acting director of the branch bureau, at the request of Zhao Xianzhang, the squadron leader of the security team, transferred the injured Xing Longnian to the Shanghai Railway Hospital for treatment. It was heard that the injury was not minor. Qian Jinsheng, Qian Lai, Qian Huang, Huang Xiangsheng, and other eight people were escorted to the county public security bureau the next morning. According to the previous situation, Huang Xiangsheng and others all confessed that they had not beaten the soldiers. Lai's abdomen was painful, and she was mentally exhausted, which was not without danger. Director Xue immediately transferred the case to the county government for trial.

All county and district-level defense regiments throughout the county were terminated on May 31 in accordance with the order of the Provincial Security Office. The seals, firearms, documents, etc. were sent to the county defense regiment headquarters. The county regiment headquarters will set up a security team of one company to maintain local security.

Wujiang County Chinese Medicine Practitioners Organize a Guild 111

Chinese medicine practitioners in this county, Jian Bolong, Wang Lianqin, Lu Baoyue, Fei Shiqin, and others, in order to connect feelings and study academics, initiated the organization of the Wujiang County Chinese Medicine Guild and submitted a request to the Wujiang County Party Department for a permit to organize. Township Chiefs Strive for the Location of the District Office 112

The autonomous regions in this county are now ordered to be merged into eight districts. The location of the district offices will remain unchanged, except for the first district office. The first district office was originally located in the urban area and is now planned to be moved to Beitang, which has been approved by the Civil Affairs Department. Yesterday afternoon (the 3rd), County Magistrate Xu convened a meeting of township chiefs at the first district office to consult on district affairs. The township chiefs questioned the relocation of the district office to Beitang. County Magistrate Xu expressed a remedial measure, establishing an office of the first district office in the urban area, but the township chiefs requested that the district office be established in the urban area because there was no legal basis for the district office to set up an office. However, Xu said that it had been approved by the Civil Affairs Department and could not be approved. The township chiefs then submitted their resignation letters to County Magistrate Xu, and the meeting ended without result.

Qingpu Prohibits Lantern Crowds from Destroying the District Office 113

Since the New Life Movement lantern parade was held in Zhujiajiao, the first town in this county, it was interrupted for several days in the middle. Recently, lantern sheds have suddenly been erected and lantern fairs have been held. Although the county government ordered the local district office to prohibit it, the general public turned a deaf ear. Yesterday afternoon, the public security bureau went to dissuade them. Unexpectedly, those participating in the lantern parade misunderstood and immediately gathered crowds to destroy the district office, the public security bureau, the entertainment field, and the residence of District Chief Wang Shixiu. The culprits are now being severely pursued to warn against illegal activities.

Jiaxing East Zha Town Shops Strike 114

The Minfeng Paper Mill in Jiaxing Jiaoli Street has been discharging sewage for days, causing residents of Dongzha Town to be unable to draw drinking water, resulting in disputes. On the morning of the 3rd, the shops in the town went on strike one after another due to lack of a solution. At the same time, many reactionary slogans were found in the town. The water and land police sent personnel to persuade the shops to open and took the merchants Jiang Shirong, Gao Zhenyuan, Wang Shouguan and others to the county government and placed them under house arrest. In the afternoon, all parties were convened to a meeting and ordered Jiang and others to sign a guarantee that they would no longer gather crowds to cause trouble. Jiang said that the turbid drinking water was related to life, that all the townspeople should question the paper mill, but that they would not dare to take any irregular actions. As for the slogans found, it was unknown who wrote them, and it was difficult to write a guarantee of responsibility. County Magistrate Jiang then ordered the police to detain Jiang and others in the county public security bureau. On the 4th, the shops in the town continued to strike because the county government had not released Jiang and others, and the paper mill had no perfect solution for the discharge of sewage.

Local Branch Court Burns Opium 115

On Opium Prohibition Day, the Jiaxing Local Branch Court publicly burned the opium and opium utensils seized in the cases it had tried from December of the 22nd year to May of the 23rd year in the courtyard. Magistrate Jiang was dispatched by the High Court to supervise, and many representatives from various agencies were also present.

Silk Cocoon Merchants in Wuxi Open Scales to Purchase Cocoons 116

This year's spring silkworms have all been placed on the straw beds, and the cocoons are of very good quality. The Cocoon Industry Association held a meeting on the 30th of last month and decided that the price for high-quality fresh cocoons would be 25 yuan per dan, and the price for lower-quality cocoons would be 20 yuan per dan. Each cocoon merchant determined to open the scales on June 4th. It is now known that the cocoon merchants in the northern routes, such as Qianzhou and Yuqi, opened the scales on the afternoon of the 3rd. The cocoon price is between 30 yuan and 25 yuan. Generally, silkworm farmers, because the price of leaves eaten when raising silkworms is 2 yuan and 5 jiao per dan, and the current low price of cocoons means too much loss in terms of cost, so they are unwilling to sell at low prices and are drying the fresh cocoons into dry cocoons. Cocoon merchants in Zhangcun Youjia, Tan, and other places opened the scales yesterday, and the price of high-quality cocoons was 36-37 yuan, but the amount of goods arriving was very small. The cocoon merchants in the remaining east, west, and south routes also opened the scales one after another, and the cocoon price was also around 30 yuan.

Young Man from Beiping Commits Suicide Due to Poverty 117

Li Yangquan, a 21-year-old from Beiping, recently came to Shanghai from Beiping to visit friends and seek employment, but was unsuccessful. Because he was living in a foreign land and his travel expenses were exhausted, he found it difficult to make a living. So he came to Wuxi alone and went to the vagrant vocational training center, requesting to be admitted to learn a craft to temporarily maintain his livelihood. Unexpectedly, the center refused to accept him. In a fit of anger, Li had the idea of committing suicide. Yesterday, he took the Limin轮船 to Nanfangquan in the 14th district. When the ship passed the Wuli Lake area, he intended to drown himself in the lake. Fortunately, he was discovered by the boatman, who urged him to disembark at Liyuan. However, Li was determined to die and planned to hire a boat to the foot of Baojie Mountain on the opposite bank to commit suicide. This was learned by the guards of the local security regiment, who informed the head of the regiment, Shen Jinghua, and the head of the 4th district, Yu Xunzhen, and sent him to headquarters to find a way to help him.

Changshu Finance Department Sends Personnel to Investigate Accounts of Various Agencies 118

Tong Zhizhen, an accounting specialist from the Finance Department, was ordered to come to Changshu on the 1st to investigate the accounts of various agencies. On the afternoon of the 2nd, he went to the county government to investigate the financial accounts and left after three hours. He then went to the First District Office for inspection and expressed deep suspicion about the former district chief's rent deposit of 2,830 yuan, which had not been entered into the accounts. The current District Chief Shen then explained the matter and decided to send a letter to the former district chief to clarify and reply in order to clarify responsibility. Later, he went to the official property office to investigate. It is reported that after the matter here is completed, he will go to various townships to investigate the financial situation of the district offices.

Completion of Three Highway Connection Projects 119

The Wuxi-Changshu, Suzhou-Changshu, and Changshu-Taicang three highways, which were ordered to be built in this county, were originally limited to military transportation, and the roadbeds and bridges were not very perfect. Now that the Five Provinces Joint Conference is scheduled to open in mid-October, and the three roads have not yet been connected, the Construction Department has specially ordered the county government here to handle the current connection work. The district office supervised the workers to build the roads, and after half a month of work, the project has now been completed. However, there is a Zhou Tang Bridge on the connecting section, which is a large-scale project. It is currently being contracted by the Yuqing Construction Company and is expected to be completed by the end of this month. However, the wooden bridges built on the Suzhou-Changshu Road are all wooden-footed and wooden-surfaced, with a load capacity of only three tons, which is limited to military use. Now that long-distance buses are running, it is feared that they will not be able to bear the weight. Therefore, Pang Shoubai, the head of the Construction Section of this county, submitted a report to the department for instructions, and said that if the bridges were rebuilt, there would be 28 bridges, requiring a huge sum of 120,000 yuan. The Construction Department will now send personnel to conduct on-site surveys and then find a way to rebuild them.

A group of sea bandits from the Haizhou gang has been extensively harassing the coastal areas north of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu Province. Yangzhou Borrows Funds to Purchase Cocoons 123

Since the establishment of the sericulture improvement area in Yangzhou County, 70% of silkworm farmers have raised improved varieties of silkworms, and the estimated amount of silkworm eggs is nearly 30,000 sheets. The silkworms are developing smoothly and the results are good. It is estimated that there will be more than 5,000 piculs of fresh cocoons. Although the cocoon merchants want to open the scales to purchase cocoons, they have no buyers. They have traveled to Wuxi and Shanghai, but no cocoon merchants have come. In this situation, the mature cocoons will not be able to be sold, which will greatly hinder the future of improvement. In order to improve sericulture and show consideration for silkworm farmers, the authorities of the improvement area went to the province to find a way to help them and negotiated with the head office of the Jiangsu Farmers Bank to borrow more than 80,000 yuan, which was distributed to various cocoon merchants to purchase cocoons and sell them to merchants. It is reported that the merchants plan to start purchasing cocoons from the 6th of this month.

Special Feature: Impressions of Economic Survey in Guangxi Province 125

(Continued) Qian Jiaju

Speaking of Hunanese people, it reminds us of what Li Ji said about "Hunan donkeys" in my life. It's true that the perseverance, diligence, and frugality of Hunanese people are unmatched by those of any other province. The most peculiar thing is that the weavers of native cloth in Liuzhou and Guilin are almost entirely Hunanese. There are not many weavers of native cloth in Liuzhou, but there are thousands of households in Guilin. They are concentrated in several areas, which are in fact Hunanese colonies. Each family has at least three or two looms, and some have more than ten. These looms are entirely wooden handlooms. They step on the bottom with their feet and shuttle across the top with their hands. As long as they get up at five or six in the morning every day, we will hear the sound of their looms, "Che Tai Che Tai", and this sound will not stop until eleven or twelve o'clock at night. In terms of working hours, they work at least fifteen or sixteen hours a day. But how much money do they earn a day? According to the people from the textile workers' union, "Their wages are calculated by the piece. They are paid three strings and two coins for weaving ten zhang of cloth, and one string and six coins for weaving five zhang of cloth. When the price of copper coins was high in the past, three strings and two coins were equivalent to one yuan, and one string and six coins were equivalent to fifty cents. Workers can weave about one piece of cloth five zhang long from six o'clock in the morning to twelve o'clock at night. However, since the price of copper coins has fallen (the price in the Guilin area has fallen daily due to the influx of inferior copper coins from Hunan, and small merchants and handicraft workers have suffered greatly and complained about their fate), each cent of silver is worth forty-nine copper coins, and one string and six coins is only equivalent to more than thirty cents. The workers found it difficult to maintain their livelihood and proposed through the weaving workers' union to ask the employers to change the wage unit to silver dollars, but the employers insisted on refusing. The two sides argued for days, and the case was submitted to the county government, but it could not be resolved. It was then handed over to the workers' union and the chamber of commerce for mediation, but it ended up with no results. However, the employers took the opportunity to remove all five executive committee members of the weaving cloth union and resolved that no one should hire them. The workers had no way to make a living and eventually failed. Now no one dares to be an executive member, and the weaving cloth union has therefore been suspended. This problem has also been solved without being resolved." This passage not only shows how the old-fashioned small handicraft owners exploited the workers, even though the employers and employees were both Hunanese, their conflict of interest did not disappear due to provincial boundaries. *

On the other hand, it can also explain the miserable state of China's inherent handicraft industry, which relies on it *

for its existence after the invasion of capitalist commodities (foreign cloth and cotton fabrics) into the interior of China. Guilin relies on its underdeveloped transportation and the difficulty of transportation. The import of cheap foreign goods must be transported by human *

labor and heavy taxes, so the native cloth industry can only survive. However, even this "last breath" of fate is maintained by the cruel exploitation of *

labor.

The commerce of Guilin has also been very depressed in recent years. The main reason is of course the bankruptcy of the countryside, which makes farmers' purchasing power weak. As for rural finance, it is as depleted as in Liuzhou. For example, in terms of borrowing, the habit of borrowing money and repaying interest in grain is very common. Farmers borrow one string of money and add three catties of interest grain in addition to repaying the principal. This is the most common interest rate in Guilin. One string of money is only equivalent to two dimes, and three catties of grain *

are worth one dime and two cents. It is usually borrowed during sowing (February and March) and repaid during harvest (July and August), which is only five or six months, equivalent to a monthly interest rate of ten *

percent. Although the Guilin Guangxi Bank is currently piloting rural loans, four agents are designated in the four townships of the southeast, northwest. Farmers can request loans from the agents, and the agents can coordinate with the bank. The loan amount per household must not exceed 100 yuan, and the monthly interest rate is 1.5%, of which 0.5% is used to cover the agent's remuneration. *

The bank actually gets 1%. However, the agent is solely responsible for the farmers' creditworthiness and whether they can repay the loan. This intention of coordinating rural finance is sincerely *

worthy of our admiration, but the impact is another question. Because the procedures for borrowing money from the bank are too complicated, the *

farmers who can get the trust of the agent (the agents are mostly local landlords or gentry) are not common in the countryside. Although the bank has this good *

intention, how can the poor farmers benefit from it? I have asked the village chiefs of various villages about the Guangxi Bank's rural loans more than once, but *

most of them do not even know that this is happening. Regarding the Guangxi Bank's rural loans, Mr. Ji Muqiao, a teacher of agricultural economics at Liangfeng (forty miles from Guilin) Normal *

College, said a few words that are worth our consideration: "It is a joke to rely on bank loans to save *

the countryside, because the amount is too small, so farmers cannot receive real benefits. For example, the rural loans of Guilin Bank, we have never even heard *

of them, so it goes without saying that they have little impact. To have real relief, a large amount of funds is necessary, but may I ask where the *

funds of Guangxi Bank come from? Isn't the money raised by so-called land tax surcharges, deed tax surcharges,... First, the farmers take it out, and then *

use this money to lend it to them. Is it not ridiculous to provide relief in this way?"

Here, I would like to introduce the Guangxi Normal College. The school is located in Liangfeng Park, forty miles away from Guilin. Liangfeng is a *

village name, accessible by highway, about an hour away. It is said that the park was owned by Tang Zishi, a wealthy gentry at the end of the Qing Dynasty. This gentry established *

special merits during the suppression of the Taiping Rebellion and was unwilling to become an official. He preferred to be a local tyrant in Guilin. The park was built by him by exploiting the uncompensated *

labor of the people. By the Republic of China, his descendants were not very successful and sold it cheaply to Cen Chunxuan. After Cen Chunxuan fell out of favor, it was taken back as a *

park. Now it is used as the site of the normal college. It is indeed a secluded place with beautiful scenery and a quiet environment. Mr. Yang Dongchun, the president of the college, *

is also a scholar who is sincere in his work and rich in knowledge. According to the college authorities, the mission of the normal college is "to provide for rural normal schools, and rural *

normal schools are for rural education." Therefore, what they focus on is how to train rural teachers, and the courses they teach are mostly *

related to rural production. At the same time, they pay more attention to rural economic problems and have also conducted several small-scale surveys. *

The focus of the survey is on the relationship between land ownership. Most of the students at the normal college come from the fields. It is said that many of them have even been elementary school principals. *

Therefore, they have not only personally witnessed rural life, but also experienced it themselves. At this time, they can be taught correct thinking methods and *

instilled with scientific agricultural knowledge. Will it not be twice the result with half the effort, and will it also be a ray of dawn for improving the Guangxi countryside?

"To go to Guilin and not visit the famous mountains is like passing by a butcher's shop and not having a big meal," a friend said to us in this way. But the saying "Guilin's mountains and *

rivers are the best in the world" really refers to the area upstream of the Guijiang River above Yangshuo. The beauty of their mountain peaks lies entirely in their composition of rocks, with solitary *

peaks standing tall, without any soil mountains interspersed, and they are not connected to each other, so they are particularly exquisite and graceful. One day, we invited several friends *

to visit Qixingyan Cave. The cave is about two li long, and it is dark inside. It cannot be done without lights. A local person is responsible for guiding, leading with two torches. Inside the cave, *

there are ups and downs, and all the scenes are formed by the dripping and congealing of stalactites. The guide holds the torch and sings, "The torch shines brightly, illuminating *

the fairy's lamp hall... The torch shines brilliantly, illuminating the fairy's cloth canopy mountain..." Seeing a slope, he points to it as Motian Ridge. Seeing a stone, he points to it as *

the Cloth Bag Monk, such as the Eight Immortals Crossing the Sea, the Carp Leaping over the Dragon Gate, the Fisherman Casting his Net... Far-fetched associations are endless. It is estimated that some of them have very similar shapes and spirits. After walking for about half an hour, we suddenly saw a faint light. The guide shouted, "It's dawn, it's dawn!" Then we had already exited from another cave entrance. After the tour, we took a short rest at Qixia Temple. *

There are vendors in the dilapidated temple. Seeing that we were wearing Western clothes and behaved like wealthy people, they regarded us as "drivers" on the car. This is truly "the utmost *

honor." However, it can also be seen the status of car drivers in the minds of the general public in Guangxi.
