Mayor Wu Inspected the New Life Movement Persuasion Corps Yesterday 126

Five hundred and five teams participated in the sports field. Mayor Wu encouraged the team members to pay attention to sincerity. According to the Central News Agency, in order to enable the citizens of the city to realize the New Life Movement, the Shanghai Municipal New Life Movement Promotion Association has organized persuasion corps from the military, police, agriculture, industry, commerce, and education sectors. At 10:00 AM on the 4th, Mayor Wu personally inspected them at the Municipal No. 1 Public Sports Field and gave an earnest speech. The persuasion corps were in high spirits and orderly. The details are recorded below.

Situation of the Meeting Place 127

The meeting place was the Municipal No. 1 Public Sports Field. The party and national flags were hung high outside the gate. On the north side of the meeting place in the center was the general inspection platform. To the left of the platform was the Boy Scout military band, and to the right of the platform was the police military band. In front of the platform, the persuasion corps were arranged in order. The first row was the Boy Scout persuasion corps, the second row was the police persuasion corps, the third row was the security team persuasion corps, the fourth row was the self-defense corps persuasion corps, the fifth row was the military police persuasion corps, the sixth row was the education sector persuasion corps, and the seventh row was the agriculture, industry, and commerce persuasion corps. The arrangement was very neat, and the whole atmosphere was very solemn.

Number of Participating Teams 128

There were 34 Boy Scout persuasion corps, 155 education sector persuasion corps, 150 agriculture, industry, and commerce persuasion corps, 120 police persuasion corps, 20 security team persuasion corps, 20 self-defense corps persuasion corps, and 6 military police persuasion corps, totaling 505 teams. More than 2,000 people, including Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of Education Pan Gongzhan, Director of Public Security Wen Hongen, Director of Health Li Ting'an, Director of Social Affairs Wu Xingya (represented by Wu Huanru), Boy Scout Director Leng Xueqiao, and American Boy Scout Executive Committee Member Wei Bai, etc.

Director Pan's Report 129

After performing the ceremony, Director of Education Pan Gongzhan gave a brief report, saying, "Today is the day for the Shanghai Municipal New Life Movement Promotion Association's persuasion corps to hold a general inspection. The significance of the inspection lies in estimating the strength of the persuasion corps itself. The hope of the inspection is that from today onwards, each team can work hard to persuade the citizens of the city to earnestly implement the New Life Movement. The realization of the New Life Movement for the citizens of the city depends on the efforts of each persuasion corps, so the responsibility of the persuasion corps is quite heavy. Now, in order to facilitate the progress of the work, the association has divided into Boy Scouts, military police, security teams, self-defense corps, and agriculture, industry, commerce, and education persuasion corps. There are separate persuasion guidelines for all work, which can be consulted. What is stipulated in the New Life Movement Covenant cannot be realized all at once, so the association is now starting with cleanliness and order. If this is done effectively, we will proceed to the second step. When the persuasion corps set out, they should have a peaceful and loving attitude and a spirit of setting an example, persuading all sectors. The persuasion corps themselves have no executive power other than persuasion. If they deem it necessary, they can report to the competent authorities for disposal."

Mayor Wu's Inspection 130

After Director Pan's report, Mayor Wu, accompanied by Director Wen, Director Pan, Director Li, etc., stepped down from the inspection platform. All the persuasion corps stood at attention and saluted the inspecting officer. Mayor Wu and others inspected the persuasion corps separately in the uplifting sound of military music. At this time, the team members were in even higher spirits, and the whole scene was very solemn. After the inspection of each team, Mayor Wu and others returned to the general inspection platform. Then, Mayor Wu began to give a speech to each inspection team.

Mayor Wu's Speech 131

Mayor Wu said in his speech, "Everyone, whether or not the Chinese National Revolution can succeed depends entirely on whether or not this New Life Movement can succeed. In the process of the National Revolution, the number of obstacles we have encountered, the number of enemies we have seen, and the magnitude of the blows we have suffered are all well known. If we want to break through this difficult situation and make the National Revolution proceed smoothly, then only the success of the New Life Movement advocated by Chairman Chiang can do it. If the New Life Movement succeeds, then the National Revolution can be thoroughly successful. If the National Revolution succeeds, then there will be bright hope for China's future. Since the establishment of the Shanghai Municipal New Life Movement Promotion Association, it has originally been carried out in two steps: first, propaganda, and second, implementation. And during the implementation, it must go through a period of persuasion, so there is the organization of the persuasion corps. Each sector organizes the persuasion corps separately, and within its own scope, it is responsible for practical persuasion. The responsibility of this persuasion corps is extremely important for whether or not the New Life Movement can be realized. Therefore, the persuasion corps bears extremely important responsibilities, both directly and indirectly, to the country and society. Anyone who is a member of the persuasion corps must first be sincere, because only with sincerity can they practice the New Life Movement in their own lives, and this New Life Movement can then show its truth. With truth, they can set an example and influence others, persuade others, and make the New Life Movement successful. Secondly, our attitude should be one of serving the society and the people, with courteous actions and peaceful and sincere language. Because the New Life Movement is related to the prosperity of the country and the nation, each persuasion corps should do it practically," etc. Director of Health Li Ting'an also gave a speech, but it was omitted for brevity. At 11:00 AM, the inspection ended, and each team marched out in an orderly manner.

New Life Covenant 132

Summary of the New Life Covenant regarding hygiene: (1) In terms of food: 1. Do not smoke. Smoking damages the nerves, stimulates the respiratory system, stains the fingers, and is unsightly. Not smoking can save money. 2. Do not drink excessively. Alcohol harms the body, ruins morality, and wastes money. 3. Do not eat snacks to avoid harming the stomach and intestines and give the digestive system a certain amount of rest. 4. Drink several glasses of boiled water early in the morning. 5. Do not eat unclean food. Unclean food should be sacrificed rather than eaten to avoid illness. 6. Do not drink unboiled water to avoid many infectious diseases. This is a very good old habit of our nation. 7. Be sure to rinse your mouth after eating and brush your teeth every morning to keep your mouth clean and prevent food residue from decomposing and rotting in the mouth and keep your teeth strong. 8. Strive to keep the kitchen and tableware clean. The cleanliness of the kitchen is the most important. It is best to have screens and covers. After using tableware, boil it in boiling water. (2) In terms of clothing: 1. Clothes should be simple, neat, and clean. Clothes are best made of washable materials. Underwear should be changed frequently. 2. Be sure to carry a handkerchief with you for wiping. When there is no sputum container, spit the sputum on the handkerchief. When sneezing or coughing, cover your mouth and nose with a handkerchief. If you do this when sneezing or coughing, people will not find it offensive. (3) In terms of housing: 1. The house should be tidy. 2. Doors and windows should be opened frequently to allow dirty air to flow out and fresh air from outside to come in. 3. Go to bed and get up early. 4. Rinse your mouth, wash your hair, and wash your face often. 5. Breathe fresh air. 6. Have a suitable form of exercise every day. 7. Cut your nails often. 8. Bathe often. 9. Wash and sun your bedding often. 10. Pay attention to the cleanliness of children. 11. Sweep the house often. 12. Dredge the ditches often. 13. Keep the tables and chairs clean. 14. Keep the toilet clean. 15. Kill mosquitoes and their aquatic larvae, fill in stagnant pools, kill mosquitoes, and prevent malaria. 16. Do not spit everywhere. The sputum of patients contains germs. Spitting everywhere can easily infect others. Spit sputum into sputum containers. 17. Do not urinate or defecate anywhere. Urinating or defecating anywhere is not only unsightly but also dirties the ground, and germs are more likely to infect others. 18. Dump garbage in the trash can so that cleaners can easily remove it, keep the streets clean, and control flies. 19. Every household should sweep the street in front of their door every day. 20. Kill flies. 21. Kill rats. (4) In terms of movement: 1. Do not urinate anywhere.

Important Information Regarding Guidance 133

Important Information for the Shanghai City New Life Movement Guidance Team: 1. The purpose of Chairman Chiang's promotion of the New Life Movement is to express propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame in food, clothing, housing, and transportation, so that spiritual life and material life are combined into one. 2. Currently, based on Chairman Chiang's New Life Movement guidelines, the immediate goals are cleanliness and order, gradually progressing from simplicity to complexity and from superficiality to depth. 3. The purpose of this team is to guide the general public to engage in a reasonable life, but to avoid coercion and interference. 4. The team's organization is divided into individual and mixed types: (A) Individual organizations can be divided into the following types: (1) Boy Scout Guidance Team, (2) Education Sector Guidance Team (organized by personnel from the Education Bureau and school administrators), (3) Police Guidance Team (organized by the Public Security Bureau chief, police officers, and health police), (4) Agricultural, Industrial, and Commercial Sector Guidance Team (organized by personnel from the Social Affairs Bureau and agricultural, industrial, and commercial groups), (5) Security Team Guidance Team, (6) Defense Corps Guidance Team, (7) Military Police Guidance Team. (B) In complex public places, personnel designated from the above teams will form mixed teams to carry out guidance. 5. Important information for the Guidance Team is divided into three types: (1) general, (2) special, and (3) mixed. (A) General: (1) Guiders must start with themselves and set an example. (2) Guiders must use gentle language and a sincere attitude. (3) Guiders must have patience and the power to influence, avoiding unconscious quarrels. (4) Guiders must be able to seize opportunities and enthusiastically guide at any time and place. (5) Guidance matters are temporarily limited to the following areas: (a) Food: 1. Eat properly, 2. Sit up straight, 3. Do not scatter food scraps, 4. Do not make noise while eating or chewing, 5. Do not smoke, 6. Do not drink excessively, 7. Do not eat unclean food, 8. Do not drink unboiled water, 9. Rinse your mouth after eating, brush your teeth in the morning, 10. Keep the kitchen utensils and bowls clean. (b) Clothing: 1. Clothes should be simple, neat, and clean, 2. Button up your clothes, 3. Wear shoes and socks properly, 4. Wear your hat straight, 5. Take off your hat when saluting, 6. Take off your hat at gatherings, 7. Do not wear a hat indoors, 8. Wear clothes made of domestic goods. (c) Housing: 1. Keep the house clean and tidy, 2. Do not smear the walls, 3. Keep the furniture simple, 4. Get up early and go to bed early, 5. Keep doors and windows open for ventilation, 6. Cut your nails often, 7. Take a bath often, 8. Keep tables and chairs clean, 9. Keep the toilet clean, 10. Kill flies and mosquitoes, 11. Do not spit or urinate indiscriminately. (d) Transportation: 1. Walk on the left, 2. Do not rush or walk too slowly, 3. Do not eat while walking, 4. Buy tickets at the station in order, 5. Get on and off boats and vehicles in order, 6. Cherish public property, 7. On boats and vehicles, help women, children, the elderly, and the weak, 8. Do not talk or laugh loudly in public places. (B) Special: (1) Boy Scout Guidance Team should pay special attention to order in public places and schools, and to the rescue of women, children, the elderly, and the weak. (2) The Education Sector Guidance Team should focus especially on students in schools, and teachers and staff in each school, especially those responsible for the guidance department, should work together. (3) The Police Guidance Team should focus on ordinary citizens and correct anyone who is improperly dressed, behaves badly, spits or urinates indiscriminately, or underage children smoking cigarettes, etc. They should also publicize the necessity of vaccination to avoid smallpox and the necessity of injections for disease prevention. They should also pay special attention to the cleanliness of snack stalls in streets and alleys, as well as hotels, taverns, and restaurants. (4) The Agricultural, Industrial, and Commercial Guidance Team should focus on rural villages, factories, and shops, and provide guidance on sanitation facilities, fire prevention equipment, food and lodging places, and lifestyles at any time and place. (5) The Security Team Guidance Team should assist the police and guide citizens in certain situations. (6) The Defense Corps is organized by the business community, so its guidance team can also focus on shops, paying attention to the merchants' gentle attitude, fair transactions, neat attire, and honest language. (7) The Military Police Guidance Team should focus on soldiers and correct any irregular lifestyles, improper behavior, arrogant attitudes towards ordinary citizens, or failure to pay for tickets or transportation in public places. (C) Mixed: The mixed organization focuses on complex public places because such places contain people of various occupations. It is feared that no single team can fulfill the responsibility of guidance, so each team can form a mixed organization. For example, at the station, if a soldier acts unreasonably, the military police can guide him. If a woman or child acts unreasonably, the Boy Scouts can guide them, and so on.

Inventory of Antiquities from the Palace Museum Stored in Shanghai Begins Yesterday; Party and Government Agencies Dispatch Personnel for Supervision; Expected to Take More Than a Year to Complete 134

A report from the Kuomintang News Agency states that due to the former director of the Palace Museum, Yi Peiji, being accused of corruption and fleeing without a trace, the Central Government and the Executive Yuan, considering that the antiquities are of great importance to Chinese culture, have not only appointed Ma Heng as the new director of the museum but also ordered the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government to send personnel to the site to jointly supervise. The Municipal Party Department has designated six executive committee members, including Cai Hongtian, Wu Xiu, Du Mengsen, Lin Kecong, Tang Tie, and Shen Moseng, and the Municipal Government has also dispatched Li Dachao, the chief of the First Section, and Zhou Songhe to handle the matter. Furthermore, in order to expedite the process, the Municipal Government has proposed that three groups conduct the inventory simultaneously to complete it as soon as possible. However, the Municipal Government is finding it difficult to dispatch so many staff, so it has sent a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau requesting the assistance of Ding Shoutang, Wang Xuequan, and Shen Xuexin. It is reported that the work began at 9:00 a.m. yesterday, with the arrival of Cai Hongtian, Wu Xiu, Du Mengsen, Lin Kecong, Tang Tie, Li Dachao, Zhou Songhe, Ding Shoutang, and Shen Xuexin. It is reported that only one group was checking yesterday and that three groups will not be able to proceed simultaneously until the court has completed its random inspection. It is estimated that it will take the court four to five months to complete its inspection, and it will be four to five months before the party and government agencies can work together in three groups. Based on the current estimate of over 13,000 boxes of antiquities, it will take at least more than a year to complete the inventory.

Completion of the Takeover of the Great Northern and Great Eastern Submarine Cables Yesterday; Remarks by Shen Fuhai 135

According to the Kuomintang News Agency, the Ministry of Communications has completed all the procedures for taking over the Great Northern and Great Eastern submarine cables. A reporter from the Kuomintang News Agency visited Shen Fuhai, an engineer at the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau on Fuzhou Road, for an interview, as follows:

Several Years of Disputes Resolved in One Day 136

Mr. Shen first stated that the Great Northern and Great Eastern submarine cables were leased from China at the end of the Qing Dynasty, with a 30-year lease that expired in 1930. Subsequently, because the payment had not been fully settled, the Great Northern and Great Eastern refused to hand over the cables. After repeated negotiations, the Ministry of Communications was authorized to take them back on May 20 of this year. Because the Ministry of Communications found the inspection of machines and cables to be complicated, it temporarily took over the reporting service first. At the same time, it increased the speed of electricity to send more reports and prepared to immediately put the machines into operation after the takeover. Yesterday, Mr. Shen, along with Mr. Boesen, the manager of the Great Northern and Great Eastern Company, handled all the handover matters. From today onwards, Shanghai can directly communicate with Yantai and Tianjin. The disputes that have been valued by the Chinese people for several years have been completely resolved in one day.

Construction of Reporting Rooms Still Awaits Its Day 137

He continued, regarding the disposition policy after the takeover, that because the matter is significant, careful consideration is needed. At present, although there are no problems with communication, the construction of telegraph rooms is an urgent matter. However, this submarine cable station must be near the coast, which is not only convenient for laying submarine cables but should also be in a place with convenient sea transportation. Therefore, the old submarine cable station near the company's Huabang Wharf is the most suitable location. However, selecting a location and constructing a building will probably not be completed in a short period of time.

Large Decrease in Food Imports from Various Countries; Announced by the International Trade Bureau 138

According to the Ta Kung Pao, the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry announced the food import situation from various countries. It is reported that there has been a significant drop compared to last year. The details are as follows:

Rice 139

Rice is a major product of our country, but in recent years, due to natural disasters and man-made calamities, production has decreased significantly, and we have had to rely on foreign countries. From January to April of this year, the imported rice totaled 2,584,985 metric tons, while the imported amount last year was 3,709,200 metric tons, valued at 47,121,346 yuan, a decrease of one-third. Among the imported rice, Siam accounted for 1,214,773 metric tons, Annam accounted for 1,185,169 metric tons, and Hong Kong accounted for 96 metric tons.

Wheat 140

Wheat imports have also decreased significantly compared to last year. From January to April last year, imports totaled 7,264,676 metric tons, valued at 60,987,192 yuan. From January to April of this year, imports totaled 2,959,605 metric tons, valued at 20,618,508 yuan, a decrease of almost two-thirds. Among them, the United States accounted for 1,804,850 metric tons, valued at US$6,446,801.

Wheat Flour 141

Wheat flour imports from January to April last year totaled 1,103,432 metric tons, valued at 15,298,766 yuan. From January to April of this year, imports totaled 166,487 metric tons, valued at 2,144,907 yuan. Among them, the United States accounted for 75,483 metric tons, valued at US$512,674, a decrease of seven-eighths compared to the same period last year.

The Strike at the British American Tobacco Factory Escalates Yesterday; Company Hires New Workers to Cross the River; Union Attempts to Stop Them, Leading to Disturbances; Three Factories Respond but Soon Resume Work 142

According to the Ta Kung Pao, the strike at the British American Tobacco factory in Pudong has continued to this day and has not been resolved. At around 6:00 a.m. yesterday, the company hired more than 400 new workers to cross the river and enter the factory to work. Upon hearing this, the strike committee sent its entire maintenance team and propaganda team, as well as the original workers, to stop them, resulting in a conflict in which many workers were injured. Workers at the No. 3 factory in Yangshupu, Eastern Shanghai, also went on strike for three hours yesterday, but soon resumed work. The details are as follows:

Hiring New Workers 143

Since all the workers at the British American Tobacco No. 2 factory went on strike on the 24th of last month, all work has completely stopped. Although the company has hired more than 30 White Russians to maintain operations in the tobacco leaf room, no Chinese workers have entered the factory to work, resulting in significant losses. At 6:20 a.m. yesterday, the company hired more than 400 workers in the Yangshupu area of ​​Puxi. The company sent a tugboat to tow a barge to cross the river to work. The strike committee learned of this and sent its personnel to stop them, resulting in a conflict between the two sides.

Disturbances Occur 144

The company's small boat, for the first time at 6:20 a.m., towed three barges carrying a total of more than 200 White Russians and workers, intending to enter the factory to work. The strike committee learned of this and sent its entire maintenance team and propaganda team, totaling more than 600 people, to monitor and prevent the workers from landing on the wharf and around the new factory. As a result, the new workers did not land and the original boat returned. The second time, at 6:30 a.m., two more British American steamboats carrying hundreds of workers crossed the river to work. At this time, the factory had already sent more than 50 Western staff and White Russian workers to take care of and protect the new workers entering the factory. The striking workers, upon hearing this, were filled with indignation and rushed to stop them. However, the Western staff, all holding wooden sticks, beat many workers when they rushed up, who were sent to the Pudong Hospital for treatment by the union. Several staff members were also injured.

Police Ordered to Maintain Order 145

Zhang Wuqin, the chief of the Third District Public Security Bureau, received a report that disturbances had occurred at the British American factory and ordered all the petition police stationed at the factory to take careful precautions. He also sought instructions from Mr. Wen Hongen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who dispatched an inspector and 50 long-term police officers to cross the river to assist in maintaining order. After the newly recruited workers were sent back by the original boat, the dispute subsided. By noon, the dispatched long-term police officers had begun to withdraw, and the strike committee continued to send more than 100 members of the maintenance team to patrol around the factory to prevent new workers from coming to work again.

Investigation of Injuries 146

When the disturbances occurred, many old workers at the Pudong factory were injured by wooden sticks. The names of those injured are as follows: Xie Bugao, a worker in the new tobacco leaf room, injured his head; Fu Youlin, a worker in the old leaf room, injured his waist; Zhang Xiuqing, a worker in the old tin foil room, injured his nose; Liu Yutang, a worker in the old leaf room, injured his leg; Wu Lianrong, a worker in the new furnace room, injured his waist; Xu Jiaren, a worker in the old tin foil room, injured his head; Yao Tianxiang, a worker in the old workshop, injured his head; Ge Bin, a worker in the old leaf room, injured his head; Zhang Jinyuan, a worker in the old warehouse, injured his side; Liu Jinzhang, a worker in the old leaf room, injured his chest. All the injured workers were sent to Pudong Hospital for treatment by the union. However, workers Fu Lin, Zhang Xiuqing, and Liu Yutang were seriously injured and their lives may be in danger. They are still being treated in the hospital, while the others have been discharged after being bandaged by doctors.

Impact on the No. 3 Factory 147

The British American Tobacco No. 3 factory on Taopeng Road in Yangshupu, Eastern Shanghai, employs more than 5,000 male and female workers. Since the strike occurred at the Pudong factory, the company's attitude has been firm, resulting in a lack of resolution and widespread anger. They convened a representative meeting the night before and decided to unanimously respond with a slowdown after entering the factory yesterday morning to urge the factory to realize the situation. After receiving the notice, all workers entered the factory at 6:00 a.m. yesterday and implemented the slowdown. The factory learned of this and, fearing that the strike would further escalate and affect business, notified the Yangshupu police station by telephone and ordered a large number of detectives to protect the factory. At the same time, they forced the workers in each room to work as usual. By around 10:00 a.m., the workers resumed work as usual.

Party and Government Thorough Investigation 148

The Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau, upon receiving a report of the disturbances at the British American Tobacco factory, feared that the situation would become more serious and difficult to resolve. Yesterday, they specially sent Lu Yinchu and Tan Peiyan to Pudong and Puxi to investigate the truth and submit it to the relevant authorities for handling. The union has also submitted a report to the party and government, requesting that they uphold justice, and will send personnel to petition this morning.

Reception for the Press 149

The strike committee of the British American Tobacco factory, in order to make the public understand the truth of this strike and to request sympathy and assistance, held a reception for the press at 3:00 p.m. yesterday on the ninth floor of the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge. More than 40 people attended. Chen Peide stood up to report on the process and the latest situation, requesting that they uphold justice to achieve final victory.

Resolution of the Strike at the Cheung Shing Motor Company 150

All Drivers to Resume Work This Morning According to the Ta Kung Pao, all the drivers of the Cheung Shing Motor Company suddenly went on strike together the day before yesterday to demand improved treatment. Yesterday, both labor and management sent representatives to petition the party and government agencies. After the authorities convened both parties for mediation, they signed five preliminary measures for settlement and announced a resolution. The workers are scheduled to resume work as usual starting at 6:00 a.m. this morning. The details are as follows:

Labor and Management Petition 151

Because all the drivers of the Cheung Shing Company suddenly went on strike together the day before yesterday, all operations were suspended, resulting in significant losses. Therefore, at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, the company's assistant manager, Zhou Xizhen, brought a petition to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting that the workers be ordered to resume work immediately. Otherwise, the company would be forced to recruit new workers. The labor side also petitioned the party and government agencies yesterday morning, accompanied by members of the drivers' union, because the labor-management negotiations the night before had yielded no results. Dai Youheng of the Municipal Party Department's Civil Movement Section and Zhao Lian of the Social Affairs Bureau's Third Section received them separately and promised to convene both parties for mediation immediately to prevent the strike from escalating.

Implementation of Mediation 152

After the party and government agencies received the requests from both labor and management of the Cheung Shing Company, fearing that the strike would be prolonged and would affect local transportation, they convened both parties at the Municipal Party Department on Fenglin Bridge for mediation. Zhu Weichang, Zhao Pingchen, and worker representatives Tan Along, Yang Quansheng, and Fei Xianghui from the drivers' union attended, as well as Zhou Xizhen from the management side and Zhao Lian from the Social Affairs Bureau. Dai Youheng, a staff member of the Civil Movement Section of the Municipal Party Department, presided over the meeting. After both parties detailed their opinions, they drafted five preliminary measures for resuming work, which were signed and resolved to the satisfaction of both parties.

Five Measures 153

The five measures for resolution are as follows: (1) Driver Zhu Xigen will resume work first. (2) The compensation for the injury to Yang Xi will be borne equally by the company and Zhu Xigen. Considering Zhu Xigen's difficult financial situation, the wages during the strike should be paid by the management. (3) Other conditions will be handled after the resumption of work.

Resumption of Work This Morning 154

After the representatives of both parties signed the preliminary measures for settlement, the labor representatives immediately returned to the union to report to the public. However, some workers learned that the company had hired more than 20 new workers after the workers went on strike and demanded that they be suspended first before they would resume work. Subsequently, the union sent personnel to investigate the Cheung Shing Company on Beijing Road. After finding that the matter was not true, they reported back to the union, and the doubts were dispelled. It was decided that all workers would resume work at 6:00 a.m. this morning.

Six Provinces' Match Industry to Simultaneously Raise Prices on a Fixed Date; Approximately One to Five or Six Yuan Increase Per Box; Already Filed with the Ministry of Finance and Requested the Formation of a Control Association 155

The Shanghai Chinese National Match Industry Federation believes that the low-priced dumping of foreign goods has greatly affected the domestic match industry, causing the business of manufacturers in Hebei, Shandong, and other provinces to decline sharply and almost shut down. Therefore, it has formed a Price Maintenance Association of Six Provinces (Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi) to save the industry from decline. It has already decided on a price increase plan, which will be implemented starting on the 25th of this month. A reporter from the New News Agency inquired with Mr. Dong, the person in charge of the association today, and the conversation was as follows:

Reasons for the Price Increase 156

First, he said that the matches used in our country were mostly purchased from Sweden and Japan. Although the price is small, it is a daily necessity, so a huge amount of money leaks out every year. Therefore, it was decided to manufacture them domestically. In recent years, the domestic match industry has become increasingly developed, and the function of the products is no weaker than that of imported goods. The products of factories across the country can almost meet the demand. However, foreign goods, due to cheap raw materials and the preferential treatment of tax exemption for exports, can still be dumped in our country at low prices. The general public is only willing to buy cheap goods, regardless of whether they are domestic or foreign, competing to buy cheap goods, which has caused the business of the industry to decline. After the Ministry of Finance issued a new tariff on imported foreign goods, the situation was slightly reversed. However, some manufacturers in the interior have been unable to support themselves and have closed down. The association, in view of the tragic situation of member manufacturers, has specially formed the Price Maintenance Association of Six Provinces and will uniformly raise prices starting on the 25th of this month to maintain capital. The degree of price increase will range from one to five or six yuan per box. This has now been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for filing.

Tax Evasion and Dumping 157

Later, when asked about the recent dumping of imported matches, he replied that since the revision of the import tax on foreign goods, it has been difficult for imported matches to be dumped in China according to normal business practices. After all, after the goods have been taxed once, the cost is naturally more expensive than domestic products, and there is no possibility of devaluing and dumping. However, imported matches are still common on the market, mostly due to tax evasion and smuggling into China. The association is also paying close attention to this. He also learned that the association plans to submit a request to the Ministry of Finance to quickly organize a match industry control association to formulate an overall relief plan.

Li Jingcong to Fly to Xinjiang to Meet Sheng Shicai to Discuss Aviation Route Between Europe and Asia 159

According to the Central News Agency, the matter of establishing an aviation route between Europe and Asia by the Eurasia Aviation Corporation has been delayed due to the frequent warfare in Xinjiang. Japanese Merchants Plan to Restore Navigation Route on the Sichuan River 160

Japanese ships on the Sichuan River have been suspended for a long time. After the last strike on the Sichuan River ships, the Nissin Company restored the Shanghai-Yichang transshipment route to transport Japanese goods to Sichuan. However, they had to transship in Yichang. Recently, Japanese goods have been selling well in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, so the Nissin Company decided to restore the Sichuan River ship route. The company's president in Shanghai, Yoneri Tatsukichi, went to Tokyo to discuss the matter with the head office, and the head office agreed to allow the Shanghai-Yichang-Chongqing route to be restored. Yoneri has returned to Shanghai and will immediately overhaul the Iyomaru, which has been idle for a long time, and convene all the crew members. They plan to officially resume navigation around the 10th of this month. Once the business improves, they will add the Unyomaru to the route.

Resumption of Yangtze River Route Temporarily Postponed 161

The company initially planned to resume all the Yangtze River routes at the same time, including the Yueyangmaru, Nanyomaru, Xiangyongmaru, Zuiyongmaru, and Daitei Maru, which had been suspended. Therefore, the company's president, Fukao, also came to Shanghai from Tokyo to inspect. However, due to the small amount of goods shipped from Shanghai, which relied entirely on the transport of Japanese goods, it was difficult to sustain. Therefore, it was decided to maintain four ships on the Yangtze River route, first resuming the Yichang-Shashi-Chuanxiang routes in the upper reaches, and then waiting for the opportunity to resume all the Yangtze River ships. A branch office in Chongqing has already been established.

Increase in Near-Sea Japanese Ships 162

The Nissin Company's near-sea division originally had nine ships on the Yangtze River. After January 28, it was reduced to one ship to maintain navigation rights. Now, because Japanese goods can be sold well on the Yangtze River and our country's miscellaneous grains are shipped to Japan in large quantities, the company is taking the opportunity to restore navigation on the Yangtze River. It has increased the number of ships to six, including the Liaohaimaru, Tianshanmaru, Daichimaru, Ten'ymaru, Wakamatsumaru, and Kinryumaru. The route runs from Wakamatsu, Sakito, Karatsu, Shanghai, Wuhu, Daye, to Hankou, with four to five trips per month.

Both the Yellow River Disaster and the Northeastern Refugee Relief Associations Resolved to End Their Operations at the End of This Month The Shanghai Municipal United Relief Association for Northeastern Refugees, the Yellow River Flood Relief Association, and the Xinwei Relief Association held a joint meeting yesterday at 6:00 p.m. at the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road. Discussion Items 168

(1) The reception center for the dependents of Commander Wang Delin still has over eighty people. How should we find a way to maintain it? (Resolution) The Northeast Association decided to end its operations by the end of June, and appointed Qu Wenliu, Wen Lanting, and Huang Hanzhi as three committee members to handle all matters. As for the dependents of Wang Delin, they should be given severance pay and dismissed; (2) The Yellow River Flood Relief Association still owes the Shanghai Municipal Bank $3,000, the Chinese Buddhist Association and Fuyuan Money Exchange $2,500 each. How should we raise funds to repay them? Should the matter be concluded immediately? (Resolution) It was decided to conclude the matter by the end of June, and the remaining funds should be transferred to the Xinwei Association; (4) How should the Xinwei Association be maintained? (Resolution) Monthly expenses should be limited to $200. The meeting adjourned at 6:30 PM.

Chongsha Ferry Price War Resolved: Scheduled Sailings 170

The route from Shanghai to Chongming Beisha is served by five ferry companies, including Ping'an and Daxing Jufeng. Competition has been fierce, with price cuts as the main tactic. Although the shipping industry has mediated and requested government intervention, it has been ineffective. Recently, the Shanghai Shipping Guild invited shipowners from various companies to mediate, stating that price cuts ignore costs and are not a regular business practice. In this time of shipping industry downturn, the spirit of cooperation should be upheld, competitive sailing should be stopped, original prices should be restored, and scheduled sailings should be adopted in an open business model. This would benefit everyone. All five companies accepted the mediation, and the price war has ended. The fares of 60 cents, 40 cents, and 20 cents that were previously sold are now abolished, and the original cabin prices will be charged.

Ministry of Railways Orders Both Routes to Use Auditory Telegraphy; Implemented Within One Year 175

The Ministry of Railways issued an order to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, which roughly stated: "It has been found that railways in various countries are increasingly using listening devices for telegraphy, which allows for convenient reception and transmission. When China's radio stations and the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Northeast Railways started, they also used the auditory system, and there were no obstacles in handling it. However, the state-owned railways still use the old-fashioned telegraph machines, which require copying the telegraph code on paper strips. Not only is the structure of the telegraph machines complex and more expensive, but the reception is also not quick, and the paper strips and ink are also wasteful. Most of the supplies are purchased from foreign merchants. In normal times, there is no way to stop the waste, and in times of emergency, there are many constraints, which have a great impact on railway traffic. It is necessary to strive for improvement to facilitate convenience. It is now found that the telegraph personnel of various routes lack practice in auditory reception, and it may be difficult to switch suddenly. However, practice makes perfect, and after several months of practice, they will be able to record as they listen. The accuracy and speed are no different from copying paper strips. Even if there are doubts about certain words or sentences, it is not difficult to ask the other party to repeat them. It is hereby ordered that the use of telegraph paper strips be abolished by July 1st of next year, and that auditory reception be used uniformly. The various routes should make practical preparations within this one-year period and formulate steps to earnestly train the telegraph personnel under their jurisdiction so that they can implement the order as scheduled. They should comply and report the preparations at any time. It is hoped that the various routes can implement the order ahead of schedule."

Special Price and Through Freight Rates for Goods on Both Routes; Responsible Transportation Specially Approved for Those Below Sixth Class 181

Article 40, Paragraph 2 of the General Rules for Responsible Transportation of Freight Cars stipulates: "If the freight is transported at a special price and its freight rate is the same as or lower than that of the sixth class, the railway will not handle responsible transportation." However, because the basic freight rate of the special price goods on both routes is relatively low, its freight rate after the reduction is often the same as or lower than the sixth class, and the freight of goods calculated at the ordinary freight rate during through transportation is also sometimes equal to or lower than the sixth class freight rate due to the application of the "progressively increasing rate with distance" method for through freight rates. If responsible transportation is not handled according to the regulations, it will be inconvenient for merchants because they have no guarantee, and it will also be impossible to charge separately on the same freight bill because the freight rate on other routes is higher when doing through transportation. There are many obstacles. In order to seek the safety of merchants and develop through transportation, the Car Department has decided, in accordance with the principle of Article 40, Paragraph 1 of the Responsible Transportation Regulations, "If the freight is calculated at the sixth-class freight rate, the railway will not handle responsible transportation, but this restriction does not apply if the railway specially approves it," to not apply the provisions of Article 40, Paragraph 2 of the regulations to the special price goods on the road. If the freight is calculated at a special price or ordinary freight rate, the road will also specially approve responsible transportation if it results in being equal to or lower than the sixth-class freight rate due to the application of the progressively decreasing method. The one-tenth responsible transportation fee will be collected according to the actual number after the price reduction. The bureau has instructed approval and reported it to the Ministry of Railways for record.

French Concession Xicheng Lane Rental Lawsuit Pronounced Yesterday; Judgment to Cancel Contract and Sign Another Lease Contract; Litigation Costs Shared Equally; Tenants to Hold Meeting on Schedule 184

The houses in Xicheng Lane on Malan Road, Saporey Road, and Ximen Road in the French Concession were sued by the landlord, Yiyuan Company, for compelling the tenants to sign a contract. More than thirty tenants were accused and hired lawyer Wu Kaisheng as their litigation agent to appear in court and defend them. Dozens of representatives from various citizen groups and rent reduction associations in Shanghai attended the trial. Yesterday afternoon was the scheduled date for the judgment. More than thirty tenants and four representatives from the landlord's side arrived on time. Ferryboat Negligence Causes Tragedy: Boatman Heartlessly Looks On 191

Empty boats vie for passengers; Wei Jinsheng falls into the river after collision; multiple attempts to save are ignored; boatmen are brutally inhumane | Municipal authorities should not turn a blind eye | The human-powered ferries on the Huangpu River are not only dilapidated and small, but the boatmen are also greedy for passengers, violating regulations. They compete for passengers, disregarding human life in the vast, wave-tossed river. What is recorded here is the cruelty of the boatmen, a truly shocking and heartbreaking event. The details are recorded below: villager Wei Jinsheng, nicknamed A Lin, 32 years old, lived at 189 Wei Lane, east of Tangqiao in Pudong. His father, A Dong, was nearly 60 years old, as was his mother. Shi Miaogen, 36, his wife, Mo, 29, had two daughters and one son: eldest daughter A Da, 8, second daughter Genda, 6, and son Qiutao, 2. Jinsheng, due to his own

Heavy Burdens 192

focused on farming. The vegetables grown in the fields throughout the four seasons were carried to Shanghai to be sold, supporting the family. Every day he rose at 4 or 5 AM, carrying vegetables across the river to sell in Shanghai, and worked in the fields during the day – a diligent farmer who never stopped working. On May 30th of this year, Jinsheng, lacking vegetables, rose early around 3 AM, carrying a pair of empty baskets (containing three cabbages unsold from the previous day), intending to sell them in Shanghai. He boarded Ji Jieda's ferry at Dongjiadu Wharf. On the boat were boatman Zhang Rongsheng and others, also ferrying passengers. The boat was already

Over Capacity 193

The boat had barely set off and not even reached the halfway point when Zhao Quanfa, accompanied by Zhao Jintao, and Zhu Guisheng, accompanied by Guan Rong, each piloting empty ferries from the west side of Pudong, raced towards the Pudong wharf like boats in a competition, vying for passengers, heedless of other boats and danger, ramming their boats forward. The two empty boats crashed like arrows into the heavily loaded boat of Ji Jieda. The force was tremendous, the tide swift. This pitiful farmer, Wei Jinsheng, was sacrificed at the altar of the ferrymen’s greed for profit, and drowned in the river. Anyone who falls into the water will resurface at least three times before sinking. But Wei Jinsheng only surfaced once and

Cried for Help 194

The boatmen ignored him. He surfaced a second time crying for help. Some passengers on the boat, intimidating the others, forbade them from speaking out, and each sailed on their way, while the helpless, voiceless man surfaced a third time and then tragically drowned, his corpse sinking to join the river spirits. Some passengers witnessed this tragic scene, but since they were in the middle of the river, their lives depended on the boatmen, so they only sighed in unison. Someone said, "This deceased is from Wei Lane." The boatman, hearing this, immediately shouted, "What's it to you?" Fearing the news would leak, they confiscated the two empty baskets and deceptively reported to the water patrol that a thirteen or fourteen year old girl from Jiangbei had

Been Careless 195

and fallen into the water, hoping to turn the death of a person into nothing, congratulating themselves on their plan. However, Wei Jinsheng had tragically died at the bottom of the river, and his family did not know. After four days, he had not returned home. His family grew anxious, as Jinsheng was an honest man who never stayed out overnight; something must have happened. His father, Wei A Dong, went to the Tangqiao area to inquire. Everyone in the town's teahouses and taverns was discussing the ferryboat tragedy of May 30th. Miaogen joined the listeners, and idlers were saying that there were still two baskets and three cabbages. Wei Miaogen, hearing this, felt as though struck by lightning – these were his brother's belongings! Combined with his four-day absence, he was convinced that his brother had

Met with Misfortune 196

He returned home and told the family, who wailed and cried inconsolably. Since the body had not been found and the boatmen had not been apprehended, nothing was clear. He hired someone to investigate the situation at the time and the names of the boatmen on the two boats, and requested the life-saving bureau to pay attention. It wasn't until the 3rd of this month that the life-saving bureau retrieved a male corpse at Lujiazui in Pudong. Wei Miaogen was called to the scene to identify it. It was indeed his brother. The corpse was swollen, with blood flowing from the mouth and nose, showing the pain of struggling for life. Miaogen, having identified his brother's body, cried and returned home. Besides the family rushing to

Weep over the Corpse 197

Wei's father, A Dong, reported to the water patrol, who arrested Ji Jieda. The Third District Third Precinct also arrested Zhang Rongsheng and sent him to the water patrol, to be handed over to the Public Security Bureau. Zhao Quanfa, Zhao Jintao, Zhu Guisheng, Guan Rong and others were negligent in their duties and careless of human life, so they should not be allowed to roam free. He has already ordered their arrest and investigation. Wei Miaogen then reported to the local court, requesting an autopsy. Prosecutor Zhang Zi and autopsy inspector Xuan Zhiming were dispatched to the life-saving bureau to examine the body, confirming the cause of death as drowning. After filling out the autopsy report, Wei Miaogen stated that his brother had died tragically and requested justice for the boatmen's cruel actions. The judge instructed him to sign a guarantee for the funeral arrangements and granted the Public Security Bureau permission to bring the matter to court for legal action.

Car Kills Farmer: Chen Jinrong Dies Tragically 198

Chen Jinrong, 46, a farmer from Chenjiazhai, Chenjiawan, Minhang District, Shanghai County, with his wife, Chen Wu, and six children, was unable to make a living by simply farming in the midst of the rural economic collapse. So, during the summer off-season, he sold vegetables. The other day, on Sunday, Chen carried a load of cabbage to Beiqiao to sell. He was walking along the side of the road toward Zhuanqiao when, unexpectedly, Liu Huizhi, a comprador from the Shanghai Industrial Bank, was being driven in his private car by his chauffeur, Chen A Rong, speeding along the road. Another car, driven by a Westerner, deliberately raced with Liu's car, causing the cars to

lose control. The car veered and hit the farmer (Chen Jinrong), knocking him and his load into the ditch, fatally injuring him. The county Public Security Bureau was notified and sent police to the scene. Due to the involvement of the Westerner, Liu's driver, Chen A Rong, was detained, and the family of the deceased was notified. The victim's wife arrived at the scene, wailing inconsolably, only adding to the suffering of the widow and orphans who demanded justice. Yesterday, the case was transferred to the local court for investigation.

County Agricultural Education Center's Frog Protection Movement 199

The frog, commonly known as the field chicken, guards the fields and kills insects that harm crops. The Zhuanqiao Agricultural Education Center, recognizing its contribution to farmers, had previously requested the government to strictly prohibit its capture. Now, during the frog breeding season, ignorant and foolish people inevitably revert to their old habits, capturing and eating them. Therefore, starting yesterday, (a frog protection movement was launched) with staff sent to various villages and fields to publicize the benefits of frogs to farmers, the inhumanity of capturing them, and its conflict with national laws, etc. Village improvement associations will be convened to discuss frog protection methods, aiming to increase the number of beneficial insects and increase agricultural yields.

Liu Shufan and Others Convicted 200

Liu Shufan, former director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation, and Si Da, manager of the Shanghai branch of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, colluded during their tenure, cleverly establishing the pseudonym "Xun Ji" to transfer savings within the bureau, using them as personal loans for trading in government bonds. The amount exceeded 400,000, mostly without calculating interest, solely for their own benefit, disregarding the damage to the national treasury. Furthermore, Yang Jianping, who participated in the Fujian rebellion, while serving as director of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, also colluded with his relatives from Guangdong, Zhao Baoshan, and real estate broker Yang Peichang. They took advantage of the bureau's purchase of land on Albert Road and Yuyuan Road, inflating the land prices and illegally profiting by 164,000 taels of silver, which they divided among themselves. After the discovery, in addition to the Control Yuan impeaching Liu, Yang, and others with official positions, the First Special District Local Court Prosecutor's Office investigated and confirmed the facts, prosecuting them for dereliction of duty and fraud. Among them, Yang Jianping fled to avoid prosecution for treason. The remaining four defendants, Liu, Ren, Zhao, and Yang, have all been summoned and interrogated, and ordered to post bail pending judgment. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the verdict in the case. Only Liu Shufan and Ren Sida surrendered themselves. Zhao Baoshan and Yang Peichang, knowing they could not escape punishment, failed to appear. Judge Liu Yukui, together with Prosecutor Zhong, opened the court and announced the verdict: Liu Shufan was sentenced to one year and two months imprisonment, Ren Sida to one year imprisonment, Zhao Baoshan to two years and six months imprisonment, and Yang Peichang to one year and six months imprisonment. All were deprived of their civil rights for five years. Liu and Ren were also informed that they could post their original bail during the appeal period.

Peideli Not Cut Off From Water; It Was Due to Repairing Public Water Pipes at the Alley Entrance; False Rumors Led to a Misunderstanding 201

According to Datong News Agency, the Peideli water cut-off dispute on Xinzha Road was resolved after the landlord agreed to deduct two yuan from the rent each month, and the tenants would handle the water installation themselves with the water company. The water company has been sending staff to turn on the water since the 1st of this month, for the past four days. Yesterday morning, the newspaper reported that the water company had continued to cut off the water in Peideli. A reporter from Datong News Agency went to the area yesterday morning to investigate the truth and found that it was not the case. The reason for the false rumor was that the public water pipe installed at the entrance of the second alley of Peideli was being repaired by the company, and the water was cut off for one hour, leading to a misunderstanding. Currently, the tenants are negotiating the contract procedures with the water company, and the contracts are expected to be signed today or tomorrow.

A Love Suicide of a Rural Woman: Trapped by Economic Hardship, She Ends It All With Death; Attempted Suicide by Poisoning, Slightly Recovered 202

On the evening of the 2nd of this month, Shen Chongfa and his concubine Shi Gengshi both took poison, and were sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. The details have been briefly recorded in this newspaper. Here is a supplementary account of their suicide details. Shi Shunjin, 58, a native of Xiangshan, Zhejiang, is the cook on the Junhe patrol boat (stationed in Wusong) belonging to the Jiangsu Maritime Provincial Public Security Team. His family lives in his hometown. His daughter, Shi Gengshi, 20, married Chen Genfa in her hometown three years ago. Due to continuous famine in her hometown and poverty, Gengshi came to Shanghai to work as a domestic helper. Soon, she fell in love with Shen Chongfa (29, originally a shop assistant), a fellow villager working at a gambling table in Shenji Li. Shen was already married to Wang, 27, and the couple lived together in the front room of the second floor at 11 Dingxiang Lane, O'Leary Road, south of the French Concession's Slaughterhouse Company. Shi, deeply in love with Shen, knew that Shen had a wife and was willing to be his concubine. She divorced her husband, but lacked the funds. Shen was also penniless and unable to find a solution. Gengshi asked her mother to borrow 100 yuan, and managed to raise several tens of yuan herself, to complete the divorce procedures. Afterwards, she rented a small room on the second floor of 68 Min Village, 311 Min Ti Ni Yin Road, French Concession, and lived with Shen. Their relationship deepened. Unfortunately, good times did not last. Due to the authorities' ban on gambling, Shen lost his job. For the past three years, Shen's finances have been extremely tight. He had been unable to repay any of the debt Gengshi's mother had borrowed for the divorce. Now, Gengshi's mother had repeatedly sent letters from her hometown, urgently demanding the repayment of the loan. Shen and Gengshi were at their wits' end, and feeling unable to repay the debt, they decided to commit suicide together. On the afternoon of the 2nd, at 6:00 PM, Gengshi went out and bought a box of opium (costing 1 yuan) and returned home. She swallowed two-thirds of it and waited in bed for death to arrive. When Shen returned home and learned that Gengshi had taken poison, he swallowed the remaining raw opium and lay in bed with Gengshi, waiting for death. At 11:00 PM that night, when the couple were experiencing the effects of the poison, Gengshi's elder brother, Shi Fengwu (28), came to visit and inquired about the money owed. He discovered that the two had committed suicide by taking poison. He called out to the residents, hired a car, and sent them to Renji Hospital for treatment. The hospital reported the suicide to the Xiafei Road Police Station, who sent detectives to investigate. They found an empty opium box in the house and reported back to the head detective. Since Shen had taken less poison, the doctor was able to induce vomiting and save him. He was discharged from the hospital at dawn and returned home to recuperate. However, Shi Gengshi had taken a larger dose of poison, and the effects of the drug had spread too deeply. She died at noon the next day. The hospital notified the French Police Station, who sent detective Zhang Chunsheng to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for an autopsy. The deceased's father, Shi Shunjin, heard the news and came to Shanghai from Wusong. Yesterday, the police reported to the Second Special District Court Prosecutor's Office. Chief Prosecutor Chen Bei San, accompanied by a forensic doctor, examined the body and confirmed that the deceased had died from opium poisoning. The body was handed over to her lover, Shen Chongfa, who signed a guarantee for its burial. The Renji Hospital diagnosis report and the opium box were kept on file for future reference. After the autopsy, Shen, lacking the means, asked others to donate a burial shroud and coffin.

Japanese Woman Commits Suicide by Poisoning: Loss of Chastity with a Married Man Leads to Despair and This Final Act 203

Yesterday, the Japanese-language Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun reported that Kuni Katabara, the concubine of Seizo Kumaizumi, residing at No. 1 Guangyu Lane, Dixiwei Road, was from Kagawa Prefecture, Japan. Suddenly, at 8:00 PM on the 2nd, she swallowed mercury cyanide and committed suicide. Neighbors discovered her and rushed her to Fumin Hospital for treatment, but she had vomited too much blood and could not be saved. The reason for her suicide was that she had met and become involved with Kumaizumi seven years ago, and they had agreed to become husband and wife. Later, she learned that Kumaizumi had a wife and three sons and one daughter in Japan. Since then, she often displayed a negative attitude, but was unwilling to separate from Kumaizumi. This led to arguments between them. Katabara had no parents or siblings in China, and could not marry as promised or return to Japan. She developed a desire to die. A month ago, she purchased a bottle of mercury cyanide from Wanxiang Tang pharmacy on Wusong Road. On the 2nd, while Kumaizumi was out, she took the poison and committed suicide.

Male Corpse Found Shot on West Longhua Road 204

Two gunshot wounds found on the body; little blood, indicating the body was moved after death. Duan Yufeng, police chief of the Ri Huiqiao Police Station, Second District General Office of the Public Security Bureau, discovered an unidentified male corpse around 8:00 AM yesterday near the power pole number 34 west of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway at the corner of West Longhua Road and Luban Road in Nanshi. The corpse was approximately 30 years old, wearing a gray long gown, a blue shirt and pants underneath, a black vest, black cloth shoes, and gray socks. Upon close inspection, two gunshot wounds were found: one in the waist area, which did not penetrate, and one bullet through the right ear, piercing the skull. The scene where the body was found had little blood, indicating that the victim had been murdered elsewhere and the body moved. A piece of paper was found nearby, with the words "Jiangsu Water Patrol Team, Fourth Team, Second Detachment," which appeared to be a communication address. Chief Duan immediately reported to the station, and a patrol officer conducted a detailed investigation. Nearby residents reported hearing faint gunshots around 1:00 AM. The precinct reported the matter to the district, which forwarded it to the Inspectorate. The local bailiff was ordered to report to the local court at 2:00 PM yesterday for an autopsy. The body was taken to the morgue for safekeeping pending identification.

Itinerant Fortune Teller Convicted of Fraud 209

Ding Hongyuan and Zhao Zhewun each sentenced to five months imprisonment. Huan Youke, an itinerant fortune teller who set up a stall at the Far East Hotel on Xizang Road, colluded with his colleague Dongfang Bo (i.e., Ding Hongyuan) and his disciple Zhao Zhewun. Under the pretext of fortune telling, they made grand threats to Gu Dehua, saying that it was necessary to perform rituals to ward off evil stars in order to make a fortune. They successively swindled him out of gold pounds and other items, causing Gu to lose a total of 534 yuan. Subsequently, Gu reported the matter to the police, who arrested Ding and Zhao and sent them to the First Special District Local Court for trial. The previous report has already recorded these details. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang ordered the defendants to be brought to court for trial, which concluded with the verdict that Ding Hongyuan and Zhao Zhewun were guilty of defrauding Gu Dehua of money and sentenced each to five months of imprisonment. The stolen 51 yuan was ordered to be returned to Gu Dehua for collection, and they were ordered to compensate Gu 483 yuan.

Twelve Male and Female Members of a Gang of Thieves Arrested in the French Concession 210

A patrolman shot and wounded a passerby with a stray bullet. Jin Jiulin, the chief inspector of the French Concession Police Department, recently received a report from an informant that a large number of thieves were loitering near the Great World, plotting wrongdoing. He led detectives Qian Yumin, Zhang Ziying, and others to investigate the scene. They arrested four thieves at the entrance of the Gong Wutai and brought them to the police station. Under interrogation, they confessed that they had broken into the Chen residence at 5 Duxing Lane, West Xinqiao, and robbed them of 300 to 400 yuan worth of property last October. There were many other accomplices hiding in 3 Wenyuan Lane, Min Ti Ni Yin Road. The detectives, based on this information, immediately went to search the premises and arrested one male and one female member of the gang. Subsequently, the chief inspector dispatched detective Wu Shungang to lie in wait inside the house to observe the situation. Until 8:00 AM yesterday morning, one of the thieves went to knock on the door. When detective Wu opened the door, the thief saw that something was wrong and turned to flee. He escaped from the back of Wenyuan Lane into Glock Road, then from Glock Road to Pi Shao Nai Road, and then across the Body Ni Yin Road, rushing towards the Xiaobeimen in the Chinese Concession. Wu the detective pursued and blew the whistle, firing a warning shot. As a result, the fleeing thief was captured by the Chinese police, but the stray bullet hit a rickshaw puller on the side of the road, who was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. In this operation, the French Police Department arrested approximately twelve male and female thieves. Because there have been many cases of theft in the area, a strict investigation is currently underway, so the names of the thieves cannot be disclosed at this time.

Weather Report 217

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong and the northeastern part of China were cloudy to clear, with strong winds from the southwest to northwest. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River and the surrounding areas were cloudy to clear, with thunderstorms in several locations and variable wind direction. The East China Sea was overcast with rain and gentle cyclones, caused by a small low pressure system moving northeast. Furthermore, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in Qipu reached a maximum of 89.4 and a minimum of 66.9. On the same day last year, the maximum was 73.4 and the minimum was 67.5.
