Letter to the Editor 219

To the Esteemed Editor: I was deeply surprised to read in yesterday's (June 3rd) edition of your newspaper about a certain Mr. Gu, a physical education teacher at Dai Youhua Tonggong School, being deceived. I am in charge of physical education at Huatong Public School, and there is no teacher named Gu, nor has there been any deception. I respectfully request a correction. Sincerely, Lu Shentong. June 4th.

To the Editor of the Local News Column: Regarding the news item "Dispute over the Champagne Cup" in today's column, there are sentences concerning the Champagne Cup final that involve the reputation of our association. It is said that because Jiande was too busy to participate, none of the team members attended, and they believed that the Guangdong team would also not attend. However, because the Guangdong team saw that the postponement was not approved, they disregarded integrity and all team members went. Is it disregarding integrity to go because the postponement was not approved? Then, what would be the appropriate course of action to uphold integrity? Therefore, the above statement is clearly a one-sided speculation that is completely inconsistent with the facts. In short, this dispute is between the Jiande team and the Champagne Cup Organizing Committee. Our association does not ask who is right or wrong. However, our association cannot remain silent when someone attempts to harm our association's reputation through this incident. Therefore, we request a correction. We hope for your approval. Sincerely, Lin Rongji, General Affairs Committee Member of the Guangdong Table Tennis Association. June 4, 1934.

Issue 12

Reading News 220

Directory Compiled by the Reading Guidance Department of the Shen Bao Circulation Library (1) Future "Reading Questions and Answers" (2) Information! 1. Future "Reading Questions and Answers" 2. Suspension of Self-Study Series

(A) Future Reading Questions and Answers 221

1. Review of Past Work When we review the Reading Questions and Answers work of the past few months, we discovered several shortcomings. To improve future work, make the work more suitable for the needs of the majority of readers, and make it more practical, it is necessary to point them out.

(1) The original purpose of our Reading Questions and Answers was to help young, out-of-school readers to study on their own, but in the past few months, it is clear that the questions we have raised have become increasingly specialized and cannot be understood by ordinary shop assistants and apprentices. As a result, in practice, those who can understand the Reading Questions and Answers are still a small number of readers with higher cultural standards. There is still a long way to go before our work can achieve universalization.

(2) Because the questions we have raised have become increasingly specialized, we have not yet achieved popularization in terms of writing. Although the writers in the Reading Questions and Answers have made the greatest efforts in terms of skill, many specialized terms are still inevitably filled between the lines. This situation often has the tendency to scare away a group of readers with weak comprehension and prevent them from asking us questions.

(3) Our past Reading Questions and Answers did focus on the discussion of general reading methods, but our methods could not be specific, and we often adopted topics with a very large scope and described them in general terms. This is very laborious for the writers, and readers can only get a vague impression of the problem at most.

(4) Although the scope of the questions we have involved is not limited to any one aspect, we have indeed neglected many problems that the public urgently needs to understand, such as commercial knowledge, etc., so that we have benefited a certain group of readers and abandoned other groups of readers.

2. Future Work Guidelines

In the future, we want to make our work more popular and universal. We must use great efforts to correct the shortcomings mentioned above and re-determine our work attitude and guidelines.

(1) Expand the scope of Reading Questions and Answers and conduct a detailed review of all issues related to books and life.

(2) Try to reduce the number of in-depth specialized questions.

(3) Strive for popular writing and avoid the use of specialized terms as much as possible.

(4) The principle of selecting materials is to start with the big picture and focus on the details.

(5) When criticizing a book, maintain an extremely fair and objective attitude, so that readers can understand the good and bad points of the book to the greatest extent.

(6) Make the scope of the questions raised for discussion as practical and concrete as possible. It is necessary to achieve the common needs and understanding ability of the general public, and to discuss them one by one without fear of trouble.

3. Future "Questions and Answers" Content

Therefore, the objective requirements for our future "Questions and Answers" content are:

(1) General review of old novels. (2) Correction of common sense errors. (3) Review of introductory social science reading materials. (4) General review of authoritative works that affect the public. (5) Introduction to natural science. (6) Commercial knowledge. (7) Discussion of research methods for a certain subject. (8) Discussion of general reading methods. (9) Discussion of various practical issues in reading life. (10) Discussion of important issues in magazines and newspapers. (11) Explanation of language and text (B)

Information 1. Unified Correspondence Paper 222

We have received thousands of letters from outside. Because the paper used for the letters is prepared by the correspondents themselves, the letter paper and envelopes are different for each person. Some use foreign paper, some use local paper, and they are of various shapes and sizes. If they are collected together, it is simply possible to open an exhibition of envelopes and letter paper. Recently, some readers have even used red paper or straw paper to write letters, and the handwriting is blurred, making it impossible to read, which has caused us to waste a lot of time and energy reading the letters. This is not to mention it. The most troublesome thing is preservation. We use bags to store and preserve the readers' letters so that we can check them from time to time. But if the sizes are not uniform, it is very troublesome to fold and pack them into bags. Therefore, for the sake of neatness, convenience, and saving time, we always hope that readers can use uniform letter paper and envelopes. Now we are preparing to print a kind of communication paper for readers to use for communication. In this way, both parties will be very convenient in the future. In order to take into account the economic burden of readers, we plan to prepare to print tens of thousands of copies at a time, and the price should be set low, even cheaper than any paper store. We only charge a very low cost for sale, and the style is also practical and beautiful. It will probably be printed as soon as possible in mid-July, and another notice will be issued at that time. We are now scheduled to use this type of letter paper and envelope uniformly from August 1.

2. Suspension of Self-Study Series 223

We have now decided to stop selling the first type of Self-Study Series, "How to Self-Study Social Science," and all other types that are prepared for printing will also be stopped. The entire Self-Study Series has been decided to be temporarily suspended. This is very sorry to everyone. I hope that readers can be especially understanding, and in the future, the guidance on reading methods will be transferred to "Reading Questions and Answers" as much as possible and published sporadically.

Special Article: Refutation of Foreign Misinterpretation of the Pilotage Treaty (3) 224

Declaration of the Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Pilotage Association Because according to the above treaties and regulations, the Shanghai Licensed Pilotage Association was officially leased to Captain Daliel (then acting port captain) on July 11, 1903, and funds were provided for him to build and establish a modern pilotage fleet. According to the above-mentioned lease contract, he has the right to do so, and in order to comply with the legal basis, a limited company was established in accordance with Hong Kong law, named Shanghai Pilotage Ship Limited.

The meeting memorandum of the company proves that the business of the pilotage ship owners, namely the Shanghai Pilotage Ship Limited in the previous 1923, has been extremely developed. Only licensed pilots can enjoy the company's shares. The company's capital is 1 million customs gold units, and the standard dividend is 8%. The pilotage fleet is the property of the Shanghai pilots. Therefore, naturally, when the old pilots of the association retire, the new candidates inherit their positions, that is, the latter obtains the shares of the departing members. In the past few years, pilots of all countries have served, and the number is limited to 40. Therefore, the shares of Shanghai Pilotage Ship Limited are also 40, and each share is 25,000 gold units. The usual procedure is that if a pilot expresses his resignation (must give notice nine months in advance), he should specify the nationality of the succeeding pilot, and the general principle is to maintain the original proportion (Translator's note: This means maintaining the British proportion of 50%).

As for the pilot apprentices, after a six-month apprenticeship, they become licensed pilots after passing the necessary examinations and obtain the shares of the predecessors. If the successor pilot cannot pay the cash to purchase the shares, the local bank is happy to lend money to purchase them. However, since the legal status of the association (Translator's note: This refers to the Shanghai Foreign Pilotage Association) has been unstable recently, the bankers have no intention of taking this route again, even though the company's assets are sufficient to provide the necessary guarantee.

The association currently has 40 pilot members, and the distribution of their nationalities is as follows: France 4, Germany 2, Denmark 2, United States 4, Norway 2, Netherlands 1, Italy 1, Japan 4, England 18, China 2.

Now China's proposal is that no licenses will be issued to anyone other than Chinese citizens in the future. However, it must be known that foreigners are not allowed to be pilot trainees at the beginning unless they can obtain a captain's diploma or other equivalent document and prove that they have served as captain for at least one year, and have a health certificate from the medical team designated by the Pilotage Board.

On the contrary, China's selection of pilot apprentices is entirely entrusted to the port captain, who consults with the management committee to determine the navigation qualifications of each Chinese candidate and decide whether he is suitable for the position of pilot apprentice. It can be clearly said here that no Chinese can have the same qualifications as foreigners.

At this point, we hope that we have already explained that if the Chinese government abolishes the existing Pilotage Board (which is composed of representative consuls, representatives of foreign chambers of commerce, the port captain, and the manager of the Shanghai Licensed Pilotage Association) and replaces it with a new committee composed of the customs inspectors, port captain, representatives of the staff department, representatives of the navy, representatives of the Ministry of Communications, representatives of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, and representatives of foreign chambers of commerce, then treaty obligations will inevitably be violated. Moreover, this kind of attempt will cause several important problems. Now let us detail one or two of them as follows:

First, according to the total pilotage in 1932, foreign ships accounted for 81% of the total tonnage of 34 million tons of ships entering and leaving the port, while China only accounted for 6.3 million tons. Therefore, it can be seen that the interests of foreigners here are huge.

Except for the giant ships that cross the Atlantic Ocean, all kinds of ships now go to Shanghai (that is, the Queen Mary, which is 42,000 tons, has also traveled around the world and passed through Wusong).

The pilots who lead these ocean-going ships are responsible for 50 to 70 nautical miles of navigation, passing through changeable waterways and crowded inner harbors. Their work requires a high degree of skill, and the huge personal risks they take (such as climbing large ships at sea) are not counted. No foreign shipping company is willing to entrust the navigation of their giant ships to pilots who do not have at least the qualifications stipulated for foreign pilot trainees. Moreover, the ship insurance company will not be willing to charge the same rate for hull and cargo insurance because pilots who do not have the necessary qualifications are serving as navigators on the bridge. In short, the navigation from the river mouth to the port is a difficult and dangerous task. In this case, the larger ships may return to the inconvenient practice of the past, loading and unloading cargo and passengers at the Wusong anchorage.

According to certain special regulations, shipping companies can freely refuse a particular pilot, but this kind of refusal has always been rare because the Shanghai Licensed Pilotage Association has always been able to maintain its high standards. Therefore, it will inevitably lead to long-term and justified opposition to the recruitment of Chinese pilots, unless or until the shipping companies are satisfied with the Chinese pilots and believe that they have the same qualifications as foreign pilots, or at least have the same experience.

Customs officials have indicated that if the Chinese government can guarantee the payment of all pilotage shares when each pilot resigns or dies, the Pilotage Association is willing to hand over all pilotage fleets to the Chinese government without compensation. However, we observe the so-called shipping bureau, a semi-official Chinese business, regarding the treatment of foreign captains with regard to the earned pensions and gifts. Without satisfactory guarantees, it is not enough to make the pilots believe and dare to do so. After all, most of these people have invested most of their life savings in the shares of the Pilotage Ship Company, or even borrowed money for this purpose.

Secondly, there is the issue of the pilot's liability. According to China's existing maritime law, the judgments of Chinese courts on accidents and errors are not satisfactory.

Finally, there is the issue of security in Shanghai. In the past ten years, the great powers have twice had to urgently dispatch troops to reinforce Shanghai to maintain its internal order. If this reinforcement is delayed due to the unwillingness or refusal of Chinese pilots to lead the ships carrying these reinforcements into the port, then the matter is unbearable. But if the pilotage affairs are transferred to the hands of the Chinese after the abolition of the foreign pilots, then this should be regarded as a future possibility. (To be continued)

Sports News

National Sports Advancement Association's Stadium to Be Recovered at the End of the Month 225

The Sports Advancement Association has received a formal notice and is now preparing for the closure and relocation. In the future, the Sports Advancement Association will temporarily move to the Shen Garden Stadium.

The rumor that the entire stadium of the China National Sports Advancement Association on Route Père Robert, French Concession, will be recovered by the landowner, the American Rockefeller Foundation, and donated to the National Shanghai Medical College for the construction of a hospital, has been circulating for a long time. It is now ripe. According to a person in charge of the Sports Advancement Association, they have received a formal notice of the recovery of the land, with a deadline for closure and relocation by the end of this month. Therefore, the Sports Advancement Association is now preparing for the closure and relocation.

Stadium Area and Future Arrangements 226

The entire land area is more than 110 acres, east to Juqin Road, south to Kangdi Road, north to Route Père Robert, and west to the west side of Route Sapey Sai to the University of Shanghai. However, it would be excessive to build a hospital and medical college on such a large area of land. The football field on the west side has been leased by the French Bureau of Public Works to build a Chinese Children's Middle School. The tennis court on the south side (behind the baseball field) will also be leased by others and continue to be used as a tennis court. However, this matter has not yet reached the stage of formal announcement, and the names are not convenient to be disclosed.

A Brief History of the Sports Advancement Association's Takeover 227

The National Sports Advancement Association was established in 1924. It was initially located in an office on the third floor of this building. In 1925, it took over the entire stadium area along the current Route Père Robert from the foreigners Gray and Glover. At the beginning of the takeover, in order to make up for the 10,000 yuan debt owed by the foreigners, Mr. Cheng Yi donated 10,000 yuan. Therefore, Mr. Cheng's contribution to the Sports Advancement Association's takeover of the stadium was very significant.

Writing Office Temporarily Moves to Shen Garden Stadium 228

After ten years of difficult management, the talk of repossession has been rife for the past four or five years. The National Sports Advancement Association, without pursuing competition in terms of actual strength, has now officially been repossessed. The association will henceforth use Shen Garden as its base, and the writing office will also be moved there. This is all the association has prepared. However, Shen Garden only has one football field. At most, three or four more tennis courts can be built. Moreover, the land is of a temporary nature. Currently, no one wants this land, so it is being borrowed for the time being without paying rent. A certain percentage of the ticket revenue will be shared.

Ten Years of Effort Ruined in One Day 229

The work done by the National Sports Advancement Association over the past eleven years is self-evident and need not be elaborated upon. The entire Shanghai sports community regards the repossession of the Rue Pere Robert grounds as a great regret. The fact that the baseball field (a general term for the entire Rue Pere Robert sports grounds) remains unused after ten years of management can only be attributed to the National Sports Advancement Association's inability to make a decisive effort for the cause. Let bygones be bygones, the future is yet to come. Whether the association can now resolve to formulate a grand strategy for the benefit of the entire sports community is a matter that brooks no delay.

Hoping for a New Development 230

From the perspective of the association's own activities, having a sports ground is not essential. The presence or absence of a venue is arguably irrelevant. However, the association's funding has to rely on the income from match tickets for support. This is why the Advancement Association needs a sports ground. Furthermore, the Shanghai sports community greatly hopes that the Advancement Association can have a perfect sports ground. Now that the Rue Pere Robert land has been repossessed, whether the association's future activities can see a new development is a matter worthy of attention.

China Defeats Xieqiao by a Large Margin 231

First-class players absent, still win by a large margin of twelve to three. The make-up match between the China Lawn Tennis Club and the Xieqiao General Association in the lawn tennis league was held yesterday afternoon at the China Tennis Court. Although the China Club's first-class players were unable to attend due to other commitments and only second and third-rate players represented them, the China Club still emerged victorious, winning by a large margin of twelve to three. The results are as follows: (1) Wang Wenzheng and Sun Linfang (China) (7-5, 6-3, 6-4) defeated Lan Silian and Kaiseisi (Xieqiao); (2) Guo Yujie and Ma Anquan (China) (6-3, 5-7, 11-9) defeated Robert Sheng and Hui Erque (Xieqiao); (3) Zhou Guanjun and Zhang Dingzhao (China) (6-3, 6-0, 6-2) defeated La Aituo and Bei Detuo (Xieqiao); (4) Zheng Zirong and Huang Jinxi (China) (6-8, 6-4, 4-6) lost to Hagesisi and Siluogu (Xieqiao); (5) Tang Yongchun and Mao Hongfa (China) (6-4, 6-4, 6-3) defeated Ma Xuerli and Wensi Dong (Xieqiao). Groups three and five won the easiest and ended the earliest. The other three groups saw intense competition, especially the first group, which was particularly fierce. The two veterans of Xieqiao, bald and white-haired, Lan Silian was the Shanghai singles champion twenty years ago and still retains his prowess. His net play is fierce and frightening, reminiscent of his past glory. Robert Sheng in the second group is newly arrived from England and is promising. Huang Jinxi in the fourth group is the singles champion of St. John's University, short and wiry, but with remarkable skills.

Zhu Kuan and Hong Yukui Win the Open Handball Doubles Championship 233

Yesterday's competition was the final act of the first Shanghai Open Doubles Handball Championship. Zhu Kuan and Hong Yukui had won every match, and yesterday they reached the final against the Western representatives Chabo and Kalianbo Aisaili. After three fierce games, they finally overcame their strong opponents. Thus, the championship was won by Zhu and Hong. The details are as follows:

First Game 234

In the first game, Chabo served and scored four points. Zhu and Hong immediately caught up and surpassed them to a score of ten to four. The score was once tied at ten points each. Then, Hong's spirits rose, and he scored several consecutive points, leading with a score of seventeen to five. Although Chabo tried his best to counterattack, he achieved nothing and eventually lost to Zhu and Hong with a score of fifteen to twenty.

Second Game 235

In the second game, each side scored four points first. Then, the situation changed, and Chabo cooperated well, scoring many points consecutively and taking the lead with a score of fifteen to six. Soon, Hong and Zhu chased after them, reaching a score of fifteen to twenty. However, Chabo then gained momentum again and surpassed them by nine points. Later, Zhu scored three points consecutively, but the result was still a victory for Chabo with a score of twenty-one to twelve.

Third Game 236

Chabo served again in the third game, scoring as many as eleven consecutive points. Zhu and Hong felt quite difficult. They only scored three points when their opponents reached twelve points. The situation became one-sided. However, Zhu and Hong's spirits were lifted, and they displayed their skills in striking, saving, and running, chasing all the way to a score of ten to twelve. Seeing the situation was not good, Chabo changed his tactics and gained a lead of eighteen to ten. At this time, the audience was worried for Zhu and Hong. Then, Hong shouted and scored several balls consecutively. He also added points when he did not serve, until the score was seventeen to eighteen. Although Chabo had a chance to serve at this time, he gained nothing. Instead, Zhu and Hong surpassed him by one point. Then, the situation reversed again, and Chabo created a score of twenty to nineteen. However, he was eventually defeated by Zhu with an extraordinary strike, winning the final victory and winning the doubles championship in this competition.

Zhu Kuan and Hong Yukui (21-5, 13-21, 21-22) defeated Chabo and Kalianbo Aisaili.

When the prizes were given out, there was thunderous applause from the Daobao team. After receiving the prizes, the newspaper team rode white horses, carrying the banner of the Guomin Daobao high, and paraded through the city with a military band, a spectacle never seen before. The Ren Bao was also led by a military band, carrying the prizes back to the newspaper office. The number of trophies, prizes, food, and supplies donated by various sectors was countless. Even the two military bands and artillerymen were gifts. The white pigeons released at the opening ceremony were also donated by the county government.

Education News

Overseas Chinese in Nagasaki Appeal for Support in the Ye Muhua Case 248

Yesterday, telegrams were sent to the National Government and other organizations, requesting serious negotiations and assistance. The Nagasaki Kyushu Overseas Chinese United Association urgently telegraphed the National Government regarding the "tragic case of Japanese students killing our overseas Chinese student, Ye Muhua."

To the National Government, various ministries, the Central Party Headquarters, the Military Affairs Commission, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, domestic and overseas organizations, newspapers, and fellow countrymen:

The deceased student, Ye Muhua, was originally from Fuqing County, Fujian Province, and was 19 years old. He resided in Kumamoto City and graduated from Jikei Junior High School in that city. He was an excellent student and received awards from the school. Ye Muhua, concerned about the weakness of his motherland, intended to join the revolution and enlist in the military. He planned to return to China to apply to the Nanjing Military Academy for further study and to serve his country. However, due to his lack of proficiency in Mandarin, he came to the Nagasaki Overseas Chinese Shizhong School with his brother in April to improve his Mandarin. He was of pure character, upright conduct, diligent, and eager to learn. All the students loved and respected him, and the teachers praised his excellent character and scholarship.

On May 23rd, at 3:00 PM, after school, as he was returning home, he encountered a Japanese middle school student who insulted and cursed him without reason. Ye Muhua questioned the Japanese student, who fled when he realized he was wrong. The next day, at noon, as he was passing by the Nagasaki Trade and Commercial School in Higashiyamachi, he saw two people in Western clothes, who seemed to be teachers, and four or five students playing ball. When they saw Ye Muhua and his brother, they blocked their way and cursed them again. Among them were the two who had insulted him the day before. Ye Muhua tried to go to school, but the Japanese students were extremely violent. One of them attacked Ye Muhua with an air gun. Ye Muhua questioned him, but another Japanese student punched him. Ye Muhua had no choice but to defend himself. Unexpectedly, the Japanese student pulled out a dagger and stabbed Ye Muhua in the left chest, hitting his heart. He died instantly.

The above situation was witnessed by his younger brother who was traveling with him. We, the members of this association, deeply saddened by the tragic nature of the case, convened a joint meeting of local overseas Chinese organizations. We unanimously decided to, in addition to petitioning the Chinese Consulate in Nagasaki to negotiate seriously with the Japanese authorities, telegraph all compatriots at home and abroad to unite and assist us. Driven by our conscience and overwhelmed by indignation, we vow not to rest until a satisfactory resolution is reached. This is not only to comfort the soul of the deceased but also to ensure the safety of overseas Chinese in the future.

Considering our limited capabilities, we respectfully request the support of all sectors of society. We await your urgent and decisive response.

Kyushu Overseas Chinese United Association, 10 Shinchi-machi, Nagasaki City.

Chiang's Telegram to Education Authorities in Various Provinces and Cities: Students Should Use Vacation Time to Serve Society 250

Cultivate Young People's Habit of Serving the Public Through Practical Work.

It is hoped that reference will be made to the regulations of Jiangxi Province and methods will be formulated for consistent implementation.

On the 2nd, Chairman Chiang telegraphed the Education Departments of various provinces and the Education Bureau of Shanghai, ordering students of public and private middle schools and above to use their vacation time to serve society. The full text is as follows:

To the Education Departments of various provinces, the Municipal Government, and the Education Bureau of Shanghai:

In the past, our country's education has emphasized textbook knowledge, paying little attention to group training and the cultivation of a spirit of service. As a result, the people prioritize private interests over public ones and are characterized by laziness and apathy, which has become a common practice. If we want to reverse this decline and restore the virtues of helping others and working together for the benefit of society, we must cultivate young people's habit of serving the public through practical work. It is essential to understand that knowledge is for the public good, not for selfish purposes. Society must rely on mutual assistance to solidify its foundation. Therefore, the revival of the nation must begin with the promotion of a spirit of service to society.

Now, at the beginning of the New Life Movement, with the aim of reforming the old and embracing the new, practical advocacy is needed. Zhongzheng believes that all students of public and private middle schools and above throughout the country should use their vacations to provide various practical services in their hometowns. Whether it is cleaning, sanitation, public places, or private homes, as well as other efforts to reform bad habits and benefit the countryside, students can identify projects, adopt an amiable and sincere attitude, and use persuasion and investigation to serve the community. The aim is to inspire society and change the atmosphere. After the vacation, students will return to school, report on their work, and be assessed and encouraged. Not only will the countryside be improved, but students will also have the opportunity to get close to real society and practice working with the public. Education will then be truly valuable.

The Education Department of Jiangxi Province has already established a Youth Vacation Service Corps, with very comprehensive methods. As the summer vacation is approaching, it is hoped that the Education Departments and Bureaus of various provinces and cities will refer to the regulations of Jiangxi Province, consider the local conditions, convene meetings with the relevant authorities of various schools to formulate methods, and implement them consistently. The revival of the nation must begin with this. I have high expectations. In addition to the Service Corps methods, which will be sent separately by the Jiangxi Education Department, I hereby issue this telegram.

Chiang Zhongzheng, printed in Donggan.

Sun Yat-sen University Education Research Institute Recruits Graduate Students 251

Compile textbooks for elementary schools based on the national center system

Application deadline is July 5th

The National Sun Yat-sen University Education Research Institute, in order to fundamentally transform our country's elementary school curriculum, has created and compiled a national center-based elementary school curriculum. In February of this year, a class of first-grade elementary school students was recruited for experimentation. Now, in order to select specialists to write this series of elementary school textbooks and study various practical problems in elementary schools, the institute has specifically decided to recruit several graduate students this summer to engage in this work. Graduate students must have graduated from a university education department. A monthly allowance of 80 yuan will be provided, and tuition and miscellaneous fees will not be required. Dormitories will also be provided by the school, but travel expenses and food expenses must be borne by the students themselves. Registration has already begun and will end on July 5th. After registration, qualified applicants will be subject to a scheduled examination. The detailed regulations have been printed by the institute and entrusted to the China Bookstore in this city for distribution.

Teachers' Day in This City Tomorrow 253

Teacher's Day Celebration at 2 PM

|Schools Closed for One Day|

Our country has designated June 6th as Teachers' Day for three years. In previous years, Teachers' Day in this city was usually celebrated with half a day of classes and a gathering. This year, Shangwen School submitted a request to the Education Bureau to close schools for one day on that day, which the bureau approved yesterday (the 4th).

A preparatory meeting for the Teachers' Day celebration was initiated by the Joint Association of Middle School Teachers and Staff in this city at 2:00 PM at Wuben Girls' High School. Representatives from various educational organizations were convened at the association for the first preparatory meeting. Attendees included Huang Zaoxiong and Xu Zeyi from the City Education Association, Xu Zexiang, Zhou Zhixi, and Gu Jiwu from the Middle School Joint Association, Jiang Jianbai and Chen Gaoyong from the University Joint Association, and Wu Zhi and Weng Guoxun from the Elementary School Principals' Association. Chen Gaoyong chaired the meeting, and Xu Zexiang recorded the minutes. The meeting began with formal procedures, followed by reports from representatives of various organizations. The following matters were then discussed: (1) A proposal to request the City Education Bureau to forward a request to the Ministry of Education to issue a notice to the whole country confirming June 6th as Teachers' Day and to designate that day as a holiday for all schools nationwide for celebration was passed and submitted to the general meeting. (2) A proposal to name the association the Shanghai Educational Circle Celebrating Teachers' Day General Assembly was passed. (3) A discussion on how Teachers' Day should be celebrated resulted in the following decisions: 1. Hold a celebration assembly. 2. In addition to the principal's automatic participation, each school may also send at least three representatives to participate. 3. Invite Pan Gongzhan, Liu Zhanen, and Shao Shuangqiu to give speeches. 4. The assembly will be held at Wuben Girls' High School. 5. The assembly will be held at 2:00 PM on June 6th. 6. A dinner will be held at Yuebinlou at 6:00 PM, with each participant paying one yuan for the meal. (3) A proposal to request the Commercial Press, China Bookstore, World Bookstore, Beixin Bookstore, Daitong Bookstore, Chen Bao, to donate books and newspapers was passed. (5) A proposal to request the City Education Bureau to issue a notice to all schools to close for one day on June 6th was approved and jointly submitted by the participating organizations. (6) A proposal to request the Education Bureau to forward a request to the Ministry of Education to increase teachers' salaries and protect teachers' status was passed and submitted to the general meeting. (7) A proposal to request all teachers in the city to vigorously implement the New Life Movement was passed and submitted to the general meeting. (8) A proposal to request the Education Bureau to send teachers in batches to domestic and foreign countries to inspect education was passed and submitted to the general meeting. (9) A proposal to nominate the presidium of the general meeting was passed, with the City Education Association, the University Middle School Joint Association, and the Elementary School Principals' Association each nominating one representative, and one person being nominated temporarily by the general meeting. (10) A proposal to nominate staff members was passed, with Xu Zexiang and Wu Zhimu as directors of general affairs, Chen Gaoyong and Jiang Jianbai as directors of reception, and Huang Zaoxiong and Xu Zeyi as directors of propaganda. The meeting adjourned after the discussions. Furthermore, due to the short notice, the general meeting will be held tomorrow, and all schools are requested to send personnel to participate automatically, without further notification.

Executive Committee Meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Teachers' Association 254

The 14th Second Executive Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Teachers' Association was held on the 3rd at Shanghai Middle School. Attendees included Wu Cangsu, Xue Jianwu, Huang Zeqin, Huang Zemin, Zhang Shaonan, and Chen Zhenbai. Chen Zhenbai chaired the meeting, and Xue Jianwu recorded the minutes.

(Reporting matters) 1. Chairman's report: A. Report on the situation of convening a teaching conference in Zhenjiang according to the resolutions of the general meeting. B. Report on the situation of contacting the department. C. Report on the assistance requested by the teachers and staff of Yixing Vocational School in Jiangsu Province. D. Report on the meeting of the committee preparing for the construction of the association's building. (2) Zhang Shaonan's report: A. Report on the situation of investigating public forests. B. Report on the submission of articles for the association's publication. (3) Huang Zemin's report on the investigation of the public forest situation in Puzhen.

(Discussion matters) A. How should the association express its opinion on the issue of public forests in the province? It was resolved that, in addition to requesting Huang Zemin, Zhang Shaonan, and Li Tianmin to continue to investigate in detail, Chen Zhenbai, Xue Jianwu, Huang Boqin, Wu Cangsu, and Zhang Gongsu should be added to the investigation team. Opinions should be formulated and submitted to the next representatives' meeting for discussion. It is scheduled to depart in mid-July. B. Location of the next representatives' meeting. It was resolved that, in accordance with the decision of this year's general meeting, it will be held at Lianyungang Normal School. C. How should the association handle the resolutions of the teaching conference? It was resolved that the association should implement them separately. D. How should the association express its opinion on the failure to achieve uniform treatment for teachers and staff hired by various schools? It was resolved that a letter should be sent to the principals of various schools stating that, from the next academic year onwards, the treatment of teachers and staff should, at a minimum, comply with the current standards promulgated by the association before the proposed salary increase standards are approved by the department. E. How should the failure to collect all membership fees be dealt with? It was resolved that reminders should continue to be sent. F. How many issues of the association's publication should be published this semester? It was resolved that one or two issues should be published this semester and the association should continue to solicit articles. G. How should the mishandling of the slaughter tax be addressed? It was resolved that each branch should be asked to assist the slaughter tax research committee in conducting investigations and research in order to rectify the situation and increase provincial education funding.

National Private Electrical Association to Establish Electrical Engineering Summer School 262

The National Private Electrical Association, recognizing the urgent need for the development of electrical engineering graduates and the shortage of electrical engineering talents in the country, has established an electrical engineering summer school to cultivate electrical engineering talents during the summer vacation to meet the needs of domestic power plants. In order to strengthen the foundation and attract talents, the board of directors decided to request the Department of Electrical Engineering of National Zhejiang University to handle the matter and hired Cao Fengshan, the director of the department, as the principal. The curriculum of the school focuses on specialized technology, rather than high-level theory. The curriculum includes steam engine power plants, internal combustion engine power plants, distribution engineering, power plant equipment, telecommunications overview, electrical engineering practice, applied mathematics, electrical engineering lectures, and English. All courses are taught by experts, and the experimental equipment is provided by the Department of Electrical Engineering and the Department of Mechanical Engineering of Zhejiang University. Anyone with a junior high school education or above, or electrical plant staff interested in learning electrical engineering, may register for admission. Students with excellent grades will be introduced by the National Private Electrical Association to work in major power plants. It is reported that the school started enrolling students on June 1st and will start classes on July 5th. The school directors are Wang Shucheng, Li Yanshi, Xue Shaoqing, Wang Guosong, Shen Sifang, Yang Yaode, and Sun Shihua.

The first meeting was held yesterday at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. Chen Jicheng chaired the meeting, and Sun Yucai recorded the minutes. Pan Gongzhan, president of the newspaper, and Hu Shuyi, the editor, attended the meeting. First, President Pan gave a speech on the issue of children's reading materials, stating that children should be provided with good extracurricular reading materials in addition to textbooks so that they can make progress in their studies. There are many extracurricular reading materials on the market, but they are usually published every few days, which is not very convenient. Children's Morning News is published every Monday and Thursday, although it is also published every three days, but the content and materials are quite rich. Originally, Children's Morning News was a newspaper that children could see every morning. We hope that everyone will support it so that it can prosper. In the future, if it truly becomes a daily newspaper, the purpose of our running this newspaper is to try our best to suit children's physical and mental needs and provide children with good extracurricular reading materials. The content is constantly being reformed every day, so that it can make progress every day and complete its original mission. I hope everyone will (1) advise on methods that are common to all children, (2) teachers will lead children to contribute, and (3) regard it as a must-read for children outside of class and a newspaper shared by teachers and students.

Various schools have ordered subscriptions from the bookstore. It is published ten times a year, with a real price of one yuan and a special price of six jiao, including postage.

Chunqiu

Records of Faint Fragrance of Imperial Incense 268

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

After they played music and escorted the Empress Dowager onto her palanquin, train, or other means of transportation, in short, as long as the Empress Dowager left the place where they were playing music and started to head elsewhere, they had to pack up all the instruments, rush ahead to the destination to wait, and then play the same music they had played during the send-off to welcome her. This kind of farcical act also had a special term, called "receiving the Empress Dowager."

I loved playing with these musical instruments, especially because I was quite interested in the history of each of them. Therefore, in this chapter of the book, I will specifically describe them one by one, like the "eight tones" mentioned in the previous chapter. At the same time, I also have a very clear understanding and firmly believe that several of these ancient musical instruments are the ancestors of the new-style musical instruments that are currently popular around the world, just like humans evolved from apes.

Among these musical instruments is the "qing" (磬), or perhaps a gong. The "qing" is also one of the "eight tones," and its style has been described in the previous chapter. The real instrument and the patterns embroidered on the yellow satin are exactly the same, so we don't need to repeat it. The purpose of this instrument is to harmonize the rhythm, making the music of the entire ensemble sometimes slow and sometimes fast, so that there is no monotony. Originally, the music played at that time was very peculiar; it seemed that there was no fixed beat, and modern people may not feel any interest in it. But the solemn and reverent tones it emitted, although they sounded very monotonous and unpleasant to your ears, would definitely evoke a different kind of feeling in your soul. This is the characteristic of ancient Chinese music. (49)

Ballad of the Lute 269

— Yanqiao

Bai Letian's "Ballad of the Lute" is a masterpiece describing the art of sound, so the Lute Pavilion in Jiujiang has become a well-known historical site. Whenever poets and writers passed by there, they would always recite the line "We are both people fallen from the ends of the earth" in a low voice, expressing sympathy for Bai Letian and the merchant's wife. Once, I casually told this poem to my students, and one of them raised a question, believing that Bai Letian was the current local official at the time. How could he presumptuously board the boat of a married woman to appreciate her wonderful skills? At the time, I only said that Letian probably didn't mind the impropriety because she was a former courtesan, but I didn't have a very strong defense. Later, I saw Hong Rongzhai's "Three Brushstrokes," and he also had the same criticism. He said: "Letian moved his boat and boarded her boat at night to drink, without any reservations. Isn't it because she was a former singing girl from Chang'an, so he didn't find it objectionable?" This was similar to my idea. He also cited that in the "Changqing Collection," when he was a banished official in Xunyang, he also had a similar amorous encounter when passing through Ezhou. Rongzhai believed that the Tang people did not criticize such things as being like being under a melon vine or a plum tree. However, "Five Brushstrokes" also said: "Although the laws of the Tang Dynasty were lenient in this regard, Letian had served in secret positions and had not been banished for long. He would definitely not dare to enter the boat of a woman alone at night to drink and enjoy the music to the fullest, and leave only in the middle of the night. Wouldn't he worry that the merchant would criticize him in the future?" Therefore, he suspected that it was a fabrication, only expressing the sorrow of being fallen from the ends of the earth, and that there was no such person or event. Then isn't it like being fooled by the tomb of Feng Xiaoqing on West Lake for seven or eight hundred years?

Many poems about the Lute Pavilion are perfunctory, borrowing other people's wine glasses to pour out their own sorrows. Only Guo Mingfu, a Sichuan poet in the Chunxi period of the Song Dynasty, said: "Regardless of whether people want to kill him, he listens to the lute on the river late at night." He also said: "How could this gentleman have young and crazy dreams? He drifts along with the world, treating it casually." He was able to expose Letian's inner thoughts.

Rice Riot 270

— Yan

A certain middle school principal, a believer in the Nationalist Party, especially admired Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Since a report once mentioned that Chairman Chiang advocated washing noodles with cold water and eating cold rice, he implemented it in the school he ran. He believed that eating cold rice was even more important than washing noodles with cold water, so he first trained the students to eat cold rice. When the students first ate cold rice, they felt very unaccustomed to it. It was cold and hard, and it was really difficult to swallow. After two or three weeks, they finally got used to it, but they still couldn't forget hot rice. The students' secret curses against the principal, of course, could not be completely eliminated. As for the principal himself, he was initially full of courage and ate cold rice every meal as an example. Gradually, his courage diminished, and once his courage retreated, he felt that cold rice did not suit his appetite and was difficult to swallow. So he secretly ate hot rice behind his back. As luck would have it, one time when he was holding steaming hot rice, a student suddenly discovered his secret, instantly making him like Liu Bei dropping his chopsticks in shock. The student spread the word, and the whole school knew, so a rice riot broke out in the dining hall. At the next meal, the students all refused to eat cold rice and demanded hot rice instead. The teachers tried to persuade them, but they didn't listen. Instead, they rioted, with shouts and the sound of breaking bowls echoing together. The principal rushed over to stop them, but he only encountered their anger. Bowls and plates flew towards the principal's head, and the principal fled with his head in his hands like a rat. From then on, the school stopped eating cold rice.

The Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 271

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 29

Returning to Shanxi with a Sad Heart, Aiming for Du Huo. Listening to the Blood Oath, Vowing Loyalty. If other people attack us and we don't even resist, that would be too difficult. With Lord Guan here, I'll take an oath first. Saying that, he dipped a finger into the bowl of blood, then took it out and smeared it on his mouth. Only then did he say solemnly: This is the ancient method of a blood oath, indicating that the words spoken will never be regretted. Now I'll borrow this ancient method to prove myself. I, Shi Fang, am now guarding Ping'an Village, and Ping'an Village is my life. As long as I'm here, Ping'an Village must remain. Saying that, he pointed with his hand and said: Look, those four words up there. Everyone looked up and saw a horizontal plaque on top of the shrine, with the four words "Absolute Loyalty Illuminates the Sun" written on it. Shi Fang said: Did you see it? "Absolute Loyalty Illuminates the Sun." This is a common saying in the Guan Sheng Temple. Now we should pay attention to it. Only with absolute loyalty can we illuminate the sun. What about you? The four company commanders all replied: We listen to the battalion commander's orders and serve the country with absolute loyalty. So Yin Deren first walked out from his original place, dipped a finger into the blood bowl, and smeared it on the corner of his mouth. The other three company commanders followed suit. Battalion Commander Shi was always afraid that the four company commanders would take this matter as a child's play, so at this time, he kept his face stern and his eyes straight. When he saw that the four company commanders had all taken the blood oath, he said again with a solemn expression: Since the four company commanders came to Ping'an Village, I have repeatedly told you to swear to live and die together. At that time, it naturally seemed like we would do what we said, but as time went on, even I, including myself, inevitably became a little lax. After this oath, we should cheer up and work hard. As long as we have breath, we can't lose to the enemy. The four company commanders all agreed again. Only then did Shi Fang salute them and bid them farewell. Everyone walked out of the company headquarters, inevitably with a look of excitement on their faces. (400)

Feeling of Summer 272

— Chen Liang

First, I saw a girl on the tram wearing straw sandals (said to be tight shoes) with bare feet, her lips blood red, her face brown, her cheeks the color of small yellow croakers, her arms exposed outside her black gauze short sleeves, her whole body's muscles seeming ready to burst out of her clothes, her left hand clutching a white leather bag, and her right hand waving a small handkerchief incessantly. Supposedly, this is her way of coping with the heat? Next, I saw two people walking on the edge of the street, dressed in green with red trim, their hats shaped like soup pots, like "clowns" in a "Western magic show." The words "Lin Wen X Flower Water" were attached to their chests and backs. They held a glass tray with many small bottles inside. It was a live advertisement hired by foreign merchants. Even small citizens who couldn't afford "47111 Perfume" could drip a few drops of this flower water. The way foreigners treat Chinese people can be described as "considerate to the extreme." I don't know if my fellow countrymen also feel "flattered and surprised"?

Dockworkers no longer carry sacks so smoothly, panting five or six times per minute. Water drips from their messy hair, as if they haven't taken a lotus shower. Not long ago, they felt affection for the sun, but now they "hate it to the bone." Running home from the furnace-like outside, my wife is taking a nap. I deeply sympathize with her hardship in catching bedbugs at night, so I don't scold her. Suddenly, I discovered a black spot on her face. Thinking it was coal ash, I was about to take a towel to wipe it off for her, but the black spot suddenly flapped its wings and flew away. How strange! Later, a red dot flew and landed on her forehead. Examining it, it was a mosquito sucking human blood. I angrily killed it. In the evening, in the alley, some people were dragging wooden benches, some were eating stinky tofu, and some were cursing their daughters as "little b*tches." I was unmoved. I lit a stick of incense, straightened my clothes, sat upright, and read the "Spring and Autumn Annals." Suddenly, there was a "buzzing" sound near my ear. I waved my hand to drive it away, coughed to scare it away, but to no avail. I secretly thought that flies like stinky things. Am I a stinky person? So I decided to "fast and bathe" to avoid these clowns from messing with me.

The above is all my feeling of summer.

Banana Tree 273

— Zheng Yimei

An old saying: "In the deep courtyard, the curtain hangs down, and people nap during the day, with red roses reflecting the green banana tree." Another saying: "The cherries are red, and the banana trees are green." This wall's eastern green, it is indeed the best flower of today.

Banana trees are perennial plants, eight or nine feet tall, with soft stems and overlapping skins, green on the outside and white on the inside. The leaves are very long and large. When one leaf unfolds, another leaf withers and does not fall. Like chrysanthemums that do not shed their petals in autumn, they are both beautiful objects in the garden. They bloom after three years, with irregular petals, light yellow in color. The fruit hangs down and is long, that is the banana, but it does not ripen except in hot places.

Banana trees have many different names: sweet banana, bajiao, and also called fan fairy, because the leaves can be made into fans and they stretch and flutter, like a fan waving. Therefore, Li Yuxi of the Tang Dynasty has the line "The banana tree unfolds a green fan," and Yang Wanli has the line "Countless green silk fans around the body," which is a very appropriate metaphor. There are many different varieties, and the beauty banana is petite and exquisite, with dense and beautiful flowers, making it an indispensable item in gardens. Ganzhou produces phoenix tail bananas, and Fuzhou has iron bananas, which are said to be grown by mixing iron filings with soil. Goat horn bananas have sharp fruits, shaped like goat horns. Board bananas bear fruit with a bland taste. Buddha hand bananas have small and sweet fruits, commonly called banana seeds. Chicken bananas are especially fragrant, tender, and delicious, treasured in the south. Water bananas do not bear fruit. Bottle bananas have a particularly large body, and gradually taper upwards, until the leaves open wide, long, large, and green, just like several banana leaves inserted in a bottle. Planting them in pavilions and halls is deeply pleasing to the eye, and it is also called elephant hoof banana, saying it is like an elephant's hoof. Many families in Guangdong plant bananas, weave them like hemp, and weave them into clothing, which is more beautiful than kudzu, called banana cloth. Ryukyu even has banana cloth, which is slightly brown. The Japanese take it and glue it to screens, which is very elegant.

Raindrops dripping on banana trees, the sound is rustling. However, when melancholy people hear it, they are saddened and moved, unable to control themselves. Therefore, the melody of Yue opera has a section called "Raindrops on Banana Tree." Football king Li Huitang liked to play the moon lute and often played "Raindrops on Banana Tree" in the quiet depths of night to relieve his feelings. It is also mentioned in his memoir of illness.

My teacher, Mr. Shi Yu, once wrote to the lyricist Jing Yun, mentioning the charm of the banana tree, which is worth pondering. The letter said: "My small building has been planted with banana trees for several years, and now it is as tall as the building. Its leaves that have unfolded for half a month are dark green, and those that have not unfolded for ten days are slightly less green. Those that have just unfolded for one or two days are light green, interspersed with light yellow, as pure as an autumn river and as charming as spring willows. Whenever there is morning dew or moonlight at night, I push open the window of the small building and lean on the railing of the small window. A kind of beautiful scenery and clear shadow often permeates the inkstone, books, dressing table, and mirror. My family only has this one small building left. Is it not what is called a small scene in a room? Wang Yuchen's 'Bamboo Tower Chronicle' says: 'Summer is suitable for heavy rain, with the sound of waterfalls; winter is suitable for dense snow, with the sound of broken jade.' I also say of banana trees: 'Now it is high summer, and the scorching sun is frightening, but my empty courtyard is like a green curtain, with dense shade, and I benefit greatly from it.'"

However, his friend Du Yu painted an oil painting last summer, inviting me to see it. In the center, a huge banana leaf was fluttering and unfolding, its green color flowing, with a naked woman resting in its shade. The leaves were bathed in sunlight, reflecting the skin of the naked woman, all green. It was beautiful beyond compare, a feast for the eyes.

"Records of Superfluous Things" has a commentary on banana trees, saying: "Green windows reflect each other, but it is better to choose short ones, because tall ones are easily broken by the wind. In winter, some people remove the stems and cover them with straw. After three years, they will bloom and produce honeydew. Those that are used as potted plants are even more laughable, not as elegant as palm trees."

Ancient people's paintings emphasized intention over reality, so many paintings do not depict the four seasons. In Yuan An's painting "Lying in the Snow," there are banana trees in the snow. Gao Qi's poem "The poet's daytime with banana trees and snow in the cold pond" refers to this.

The monk Huai Su learned calligraphy without paper, so he planted ten thousand banana trees for writing, calling his residence the Green Sky Hermitage. Also, Zhao Chun, of the Southern Han Dynasty, planted banana trees in his pavilions and halls, which were called "Banana Tree Fanatic." He can be compared to He Jing's plums, Yuan Ming's chrysanthemums, Lian Xi's lotuses, and Zi Lian's bamboos, all beautiful for thousands of years.

"Tough Gourd Collection" says: Someone once summoned a fairy, putting a banana leaf in his sleeve. When asked to write a poem about it, the fairy wrote: "Deeply hidden in the sleeve is a green leaf, knowing that you intend to insult the divine spirit. Tonight, try listening to the rain on the banana tree, dripping for a long time, with a double sound." The mythology of the banana tree is enough for conversation.

Banana trees can be divided into small plants for planting. If you use a hairpin to pierce two holes to let out the air, they will be short and graceful, never growing tall, which is what you want for potted plants.

Free Talk

On Deception 274

— Dong Ruo

Deception is usually regarded as an immoral thing, but in our society, there are endless facts of deception. Therefore, in our newspapers, we can get many records of deception every day. The law considers some deceptions, such as the abduction of women and the defrauding of money, as criminal acts, and imposes severe punishments and heavy fines. However, this cannot eliminate or reduce the occurrence of deception.

Why is this? Is it because deceptive people have a dishonest nature? Is it because people like Long Bu and Luo Su have skulls with unavoidable criminal behavior, as they said? The question does not seem to be that simple. Here, we should first examine the nature of deception. Obviously, deception is a distortion of facts, a conscious distortion in an attempt to achieve some benefit, directly or indirectly obtaining some benefit from the object being deceived. Therefore, the act of deception itself carries the division and contradiction between the deceiver and the deceived. Therefore, in a society, if the molecules that make up its interior contradict and conflict with each other more in terms of interests, the task played by deception will become more complex and important. Based on this, we can know that the reason why there are more deception incidents in the cities of capitalist societies than in feudal societies is not simply due to the frequent contact between individuals, but the most important reason is that individualism, free competition, and the contradictions and conflicts between people under capitalism have deepened compared to the previous feudal society.

Knowing that deception is not due to people's dishonest nature, or some innate criminal skull, but the social basis on which it occurs, we can easily understand further: deception is not only the use of one person by another, but sometimes even becomes one of the weapons of one group against another group. When Country A and Country B are at daggers drawn, Country A uses its own news agency to spread rumors, saying that Country B's border troops have mutinied. When two political parties compete in an election, they each issue empty checks to the public and raise the banner of seeking welfare for the people. Aren't these all acts of deception?

Because deception plays a huge role in this society, the art of deception is very necessary to study. A person wearing tattered clothes woos a noble lady, saying that he has a huge fortune at home. This is a deception that anyone can detect, and it is simply not worth talking about as an art.

The highest art of deception is a great truth on the surface, but with deception as its core.

This highest art of deception has been used by the powerful throughout human history...

(1) The debate on short essays has a tendency to "the more you argue, the more chaotic it becomes." After publishing "How Should We Say It?" and "Each Doing Their Best" in the previous issue, this journal plans to no longer publish articles related to this debate. We hope that contributors will understand!

(2) This journal has limited space and cannot publish many long novels. There are also many manuscripts in stock. Please do not send any more manuscripts for the time being.

(3) Manuscripts will not be returned as a rule. However, if contributors believe that their works are valuable and attach an envelope with the return address clearly written and sufficient postage affixed when submitting the manuscript, this journal will try its best to send it back. If contributors do not send manuscripts in accordance with this method and request them by letter, it will be difficult to comply. We respectfully ask for your understanding.

Mourning Lu Yin (Continued) 276

— Lanru, sent from Changsha

It was the winter before last year when I went to Sandefang to see Xiao Lu. She said to me:

"Xiao Bing, you should go see Lu Yin. She was still asking about you last time she came. She's in a pitiful state now, you should go see her."

"What? Pitiful? Isn't she already married to her little lover and living happily?"

I was greatly surprised to hear her say that she was pitiful.

"Although marriage is happy, the children keep coming, which is killing her!"

"How many has she had now?"

"Although there are only two, she's already..."

I knew what the unspoken words were.

"Alas! Too painful! That's more painful and dangerous than giving birth."

"Isn't it? She said it's so boring and painful to be a woman, it's better to be dead than alive."

I made up my mind several times to go see her, and once I even made an appointment with Ms. Huiqun to have dinner at her house first, then go see Lu Yin, and then everyone go to the arts and crafts fair at the Shanghai Municipal Council Girls' School. Later, I don't know what happened temporarily, and I broke the appointment. I didn't go to Huiqun's house for dinner, but we eventually ran into each other at the fair.

"Where's Lu Yin?" I asked Huiqun.

"She's right in front, did you see her? There, the one wearing the gray qipao is her."

Following her finger, I saw a thin, haggard profile in the distance, and I couldn't help but sigh.

"Do you want to find her?" Huiqun asked me.

"No, there are too many people here, it's not easy to talk. I'll go see her another day."

Alas! Who knew that missing that opportunity to meet, I would never see her again!

Lu Yin, you have gained liberation and left this painful world far behind. But in the nether world, did you ever think of the sadness of your husband and daughter? The three-year-old child, although she doesn't know that you are dead, she thinks you are sleeping and will wake up later. But the misery of this ignorant child is even more heartbreaking!

Lu Yin, because of your death, I was reminded of two good friends, one is Binzhi, whose disappearance and tragic death is known to everyone, and the other is Bingzhi, the late wife of Mr. Lie Wen, who died of the same disease as you. You and Bingzhi were both misdiagnosed by incompetent doctors, which is truly heartbreaking. How insignificant is a woman's life, either dying under knives and guns or being lost in childbirth. I am not someone who enjoys life and fears death, but people who have made considerable contributions to society and have hopes in literature should not die so easily. Your deaths are not only a loss to literature but also a loss to society!

As I write this, it is already the time for the first watch. It is raining heavily outside, with thunder rumbling. I put down my pen and stared blankly at the lightning-flashing sky. Two tears fell from my eyes.

Lu Yin, if you are conscious after death, you should understand my current mood! (End)

Originally the Old Site of Lingguang 277

— Bai Ge

Anyone who goes to Qufu to seek the traces of the sages will likely visit the Temple of the Duke of Zhou. First, the Duke of Zhou can also be considered a sage, and he was a sage who inherited from the past and ushered in the future after Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, and Wu, and before Confucius. It is said that he has a certain position in the orthodox lineage of Confucianism. Secondly, it is said that the current Temple of the Duke of Zhou is the old site of the Lingguang Hall, a place of great righteousness and brilliance. In this way, a desire to visit is naturally formed in the hearts of people who have been baptized by Confucianism.

The temple seems to be outside the East Gate, right? In any case, when I went, I went out from the East Gate. I heard that the former State of Lu was outside this East Gate, with the temple as the center, while the Qufu with the Temple of Confucius as the center was the countryside of the State of Lu at that time. If the Lingguang Hall was within the city of Lu, then Lu could be considered a large country after all. Because going from the East Gate to the Temple of the Duke of Zhou, one has to pass through a vast field.

From the outside, especially standing a little further away, the temple does look like a majestic palace. Uneven ancient trees thickly shade the top of the temple, and in some places, a piece of tiled ridge is sparsely visible. If a few red leaves are added in late autumn, the scenery is somewhat moving. The surrounding red walls have long been dilapidated; one can enter without necessarily going through the gate, so there is no one guarding the temple gate, nor is there any greeting or disturbance to those who enter. Often, a solemn feeling is evoked from a gloomy feeling.

As soon as one enters the gate, the dusty walls and broken windows of the three bays and two corridors, and the overgrown weeds on the small path, all present a desolate scene. Walking in the middle, there is a monument beside the path, erected by Emperor Qianlong or someone else. I don't remember the inscription on it very clearly, I only remember that the second sentence is "Originally the old site of Lingguang," and the rest are some praises, giving visitors an example to believe that this place is the old site of Lingguang Hall. It is unexpected that such a famous place at that time has now become like this. It is no wonder that the disciples of the sages are sighing that rituals are not promoted and need to be restored.

Going up another level is the main hall where the Duke of Zhou lived. It seems that only the Duke of Zhou is sitting in the middle; unlike Confucius, who has many disciples standing on both sides accompanying him, which naturally makes people feel a little too lonely. Although we have never dreamed of what kind of person the Duke of Zhou was, as soon as we see the clay sculpture, we feel as if we have seen him before. A kind of demeanor with a very strong sense of morality, just like the dignified old scholars we often see on the stage. His face is white, and mostly carries some scholarly air. China has always had a warning for scholars who will eventually become officials: "Scholars should not have scholarly air." It seems that it is natural that such a Duke of Zhou is not loved. However, recently the government has decided to allocate a portion of the funds from the national treasury, even when it is in financial difficulty, to repair the temples of Confucius, Mencius, Yan Hui, and the Duke of Zhou, which surprisingly shows an intention to promote scholarly air.

To pay homage to the traces of the sages, one should first go with a heart of admiration. The reason why many ancient places and cities arouse our longing and lingering is mostly because we first have a heart of nostalgia and admiration. What is there about the Duke of Zhou that is worthy of our admiration? What is there about Lingguang Hall that is worthy of our nostalgia and lingering? So, I had no choice but to walk out of the ancient temple gate indifferently, with silent footsteps.

Returning from the "Bamboo Creek Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition" 278

— Mu Mutian

"Perhaps in the future, square characters will be abolished altogether, and Chinese characters will be Latinized. But until now, calligraphy is still a kind of art. When doing research on the history of art, calligraphy is also an object." After watching the "Bamboo Creek Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition" and returning from the Lake Society, I thought this way on the way.

The "Bamboo Creek Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition" includes more than 300 works, including the calligraphy of Mr. Shen Yinmo and the paintings of Mr. Shen Maishi. Perhaps because of a special understanding of people, I focused my attention almost entirely on the calligraphy of Mr. Shen Yinmo. Although I often saw Mr. Shen Yinmo's calligraphy in Beijing a few years ago, I had never seen such a rich output as it is now.

However, the quality of artworks cannot be judged by their quantity; the main thing is to see how good they are in quality. I have not studied in detail what kind of society the art of calligraphy is a product of. However, just as classical tragedies have a unique beauty, the art of calligraphy also has its unique beauty. We can study the art of calligraphy from a sociological standpoint. But now is not the time; we don't have that kind of time to spare. However, even now, when we don't have time to consider those issues, we can still see whether calligraphy is good or bad. Art that has life, art that has the creator's creative loyalty, no matter which historical stage it is a product of, will always be moving.

Before Dawn 279

— Cheng Yunping

(1) The pitch-black night occupies our village: the collapsing broken houses rustle in the wind, the nightingale sings softly in the desolate forest, and nocturnal beasts wander in the barren fields. (2) The pitch-black night occupies our village: sleeping people are muttering nonsense, lonely men and women are shedding tears of sorrow by their pillows, and sleepless farmers are anxiously waiting for dawn. (3) Suddenly, the hoarse rooster stretches its neck and crows loudly, startling the lazy people awake from their dreams. The beasts flee into their dens, the nightingale stops singing, and a line of dawn is faintly rising on the horizon!

Fire Disaster (1) 280

— Fei

In the winter of this year, I traveled to Nanyang for the second time. I ran from the Philippines, Borneo, and Java to Sumatra. I was much more familiar with Sumatra. About ten years ago, I worked as a secretary in a small place under Deli (1), in the store of my uncle Guan Youguang. I like traveling very much, and I have been to almost all the nearby places. If someone were to ask me to be a guide for a trip to Sumatra now, I would be very satisfied. In addition to traveling, I also had some missions this time: a certain overseas Chinese school in China entrusted me to investigate the current situation of overseas Chinese schools in Nanyang, especially at this time when Nanyang has been hit by the economic panic, and the foundations of overseas Chinese schools are mostly shaken. Also, a certain art and book company entrusted me to take pictures of some scenic spots, historical sites, buildings, and other things in Nanyang and send them to them, in preparation for compiling a Nanyang pictorial. So, along the way, in addition to sightseeing, I also did various tasks of investigation and photography. In my luggage, a lot of manuscripts and pictures have already accumulated. For this mysterious land of the shining sun, the value of these things is not small.

Arriving in Medan (2), I finished my work. I thought about going to the high mountain of Berastagi to take some scenic photos, and then going around from the central part of Sumatra to Dolok Silau to visit my old residence ten years ago, to see how my relatives have been, and to see how my childhood friends are now. At this time, the pre-economic panic in Nanyang had deepened, and it was completely different from the golden world when I lived here ten years ago. This, I have already clearly seen the declining scene in other places. Alas, Dolok Silau, this small commercial port, how have you been gripped by the iron palm of "recession"? My old friends and compatriots who are still struggling here, what kind of beating have you been subjected to by this ruthless tyrant?

With this feeling in mind, I arrived at my destination on the afternoon of the day after leaving Berastagi. Alas, where have the bustling vehicles of the past gone? Why are there so few pedestrians on the road? Passing by the restaurants, why can't I hear the noise of the overseas Chinese gathering to gamble and relax as before? When I got out of the long-distance bus and stepped under the black-lettered signboard of Qunyuhao opened by my relatives, a cold, gloomy air startled me. (At that time, the sun was still shining brightly, and the sunlight was still hot and scorching in the tropics.) Glancing into the store, there was only a clerk dozing off quietly, and two or three natives were sitting on the floor, muttering. Ah! How did the buyers and sellers who used to be overwhelmed with business become so quiet? In the past, it was completely different. At that time, the busy business was enough to make a clerk's waist ache and hands hurt, where would there be free time for you to sit down and rest? Let alone let you doze off?

Grain and Flour Futures Rise and Then Fall Sharply 294

Yesterday's flour market saw significant fluctuations after the morning opening. The Chicago and Canadian quotations for foreign wheat jumped by a substantial 1.12 yuan, so the opening price for the current month was stable, with little change from the previous week. This triggered enthusiastic buying from external speculators, pushing prices higher. For example, the September and October contracts rose by about 0.2 to 0.3 yuan compared to the previous week. However, this rise created a good opportunity for manufacturers to sell large quantities, causing prices to fall sharply in subsequent trading. In the afternoon, during the first two trades, long positions tried hard to compete, but their momentum waned. As buying interest decreased and factories sold off forward contracts, the market gradually declined. The rise was purely speculative, and the arrival of new wheat will bring many changes. As a result, the current month fell by 0.175 yuan, July fell by 0.075 yuan, August fell by 0.1 yuan, September fell by 0.15 yuan, and October and November each fell by 0.0325 yuan.

Wheat Futures: High in the Morning, Low in the Afternoon 295

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw rising prices after the morning opening. Although foreign wheat quotations fell slightly by 1.12 yuan, the poor harvests abroad seemed to have triggered speculation from outside investors. This situation was similar to the major floods in China in previous years. Therefore, buying interest was very strong in each trade, with prices rising by 0.3 to 0.6 yuan compared to the closing price of the previous week. However, in the afternoon, the market suddenly weakened, as flour futures did not rise but fell, seemingly shaking the foundation. Opening prices dropped by 0.3 to 0.5 yuan, and the market hovered as selling pressure eased. Given the abundant harvest of new wheat in China, it will be difficult to raise grain prices again in the short term. As a result, July fell by 0.02 yuan, August remained unchanged, September fell by 0.02 yuan, and October fell by 0.01 yuan. Spot wheat remained unchanged as factories did not move and there were no new transactions.

The asking price was four yuan and two jiao, but buyers did not agree to the price difference of two jiao, so no transaction was made.

Oil Market: Hong White Tung Oil Trending Higher 301
